Fuzhou Financial Relief Association Established: Sixty to Seventy Merchants Apply for Mortgages; Only a Few Qualify for Loans 61

Fuzhou Dispatch: After the establishment of the Fuzhou Financial Relief Committee, the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications have allocated 1 million legal tender to be loaned to merchants through the Provincial Bank. Recently, sixty to seventy merchants have brought their property deeds to the Relief Association to apply for mortgages. However, the conditions set by the association are very strict:

The property must be owned by the applicant.

The property must be insured against fire.

The deed must have been taxed and registered with the court.

Repayment must be guaranteed by a merchant shop with substantial capital.

As a result, only a few have qualified for loans. However, the Southeast Bank has received 150,000 yuan and will begin disbursing 50% of the banknotes on the 20th. Tianji Money Exchange will also begin disbursing 50% of the banknotes on the 22nd. The remaining 50% will be disbursed on a regular basis after debt settlement. Small insurance companies have also borrowed 70,000 yuan for lending to policyholders. The money exchanges originally planned to borrow 300,000 yuan from the Provincial Bank to lend to merchants. Now, due to the excessively strict conditions set by the Financial Relief Association, they fear taking responsibility and have stopped borrowing. As for the merchants, they are divided into two factions. Those with real estate to mortgage are asking the Relief Association to change the loan methods: 1. Remove the merchant shop guarantee. 2. Provide loans first and then register. It is unknown if this will be approved. However, there are only a few days left until the end of the year, and most merchants have not received the loans, so they are very anxious. Those without real estate to mortgage believe that the tightness of money this year is many times worse than in previous years. The meager 800,000 yuan (because 150,000 yuan for the Southeast Bank and 70,000 yuan for small insurance are unrelated to the merchants) cannot provide relief. Yesterday, they jointly requested the County Chamber of Commerce to allow the closing period to be extended to the second day of the second month of the lunar new year. Two-thirds would be repaid at the end of the lunar year, and the remainder would be settled when due. However, this is inconsistent with business customs and is unlikely to be realized. Furthermore, Fuzhou's commercial decline last year reached its peak. Exports of all kinds of special products such as tea, wood, paper, and bamboo shoots have plummeted. Nine out of ten shops are losing money. It is expected that more tea, wood, paper, and bamboo shoot merchants will close down this year than last year. The Jiangsu-Guangdong guilds and silk and cloth guilds have decided to reduce their scale uniformly starting next lunar year, laying off some shop assistants or reducing salaries. The Yunwen and Jiulong stores on South Street in the city have already implemented this first. Therefore, the shop assistants of general stores are worried about unemployment and are extremely anxious. However, in the administrative and education sectors, the funds coordinated by the Ministry of Finance and Education have been remitted in advance. January salaries can be paid on the 21st, which is quite optimistic. As for the poor, charitable organizations in previous years have all organized end-of-year assistance. This year, due to the depression of commercial activities, it is not easy to donate money, and all organizations have suspended it. However, the Provincial New Sports Association, the Provincial Relief Association, the Red Cross Society, and the Red Swastika Society are jointly organizing winter relief: Each person will receive four jiao of silver, and each person will receive five sheng of white rice, limited to 5,000 people. (January 18th)

Bandit Liu's Rampant Activities: Gathers Bandits from Outside the Pass, Plans to Flee South, Incited by Some Party, Briefly Captures Laiyuan 62

Tianjin Dispatch: Liu Guitang recently gathered bandits on the border of Hebei and Chahar, including Zhang Haijiao and Da Wanglong outside the Great Wall. He also gathered Fei Yun, Wang Yanru and other bandits as well as two companies of cavalry from Xia Ziming's regiment, which had defected in eastern Chahar, using the Yanhai, Sihai, and Yongning Forts of Yanqing as bases. They are receiving supplies of guns and ammunition from a certain country and changing into blue cloth uniforms and wearing the East Asian Alliance emblem. They are divided into several groups and fleeing south across the Great Wall, wanting to use the old route of the 23rd Army to reach the junction of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan, to join forces with Liu Zhinan, Zhao Dehuai, and other bandit gangs in western Shandong, northern Henan, and southern Hebei to launch a major operation. Since the winter solstice, Liu himself led an army of thousands, intending to cross southwest to Hebei, but was repeatedly blocked by the 29th and 50th Army units and failed. The bandits then fled back to western Hebei, intending to enter Yuxian County in Chahar Province and go west to western Suiyuan, to invade Inner Mongolia. Just as they were fleeing to the border of Yuxian County, they were intercepted by Dong Shengtang's regiment of Zhang Zizhong's division of the 29th Army. At the same time, the Jin army, fearing the bandits would flee into their territory, sent a regiment to intercept them near Longquanguan. The bandits were forced to turn back south again. The majority have returned to their old nest in the Yanhai and Sihai areas of Yanqing, lying low and waiting for an opportunity. Jin Huanwen (Liu's chief of staff) is leading 1,000 men from Fei Yun, including 400 cavalry and 700 infantry, carrying five steel cannons and over ten light and heavy machine guns. On the 5th, they fled to Wulonggou in Yixian County, and on the 6th, they fled to Majiacun. Having heard that the main force of the 29th Army was coming from Quyang to suppress them, they returned to take advantage of the emptiness, and on the evening of the 7th, they attacked and entered Laiyuan County. The county's local defense forces were weak, so the bandits were allowed to enter the city. The county magistrate and the chief of public security took the seal and fled to Lingqiu, Jin, to conduct their affairs. On the one hand, they telegraphed the province for help. After the bandits occupied Laiyuan, the cavalry were stationed outside the city, and the infantry were stationed inside the city. Villages within thirty miles of the county seat were raped and looted. The wealthy families in the city were all searched, and hundreds of men and women were kidnapped for ransom. The chamber of commerce president was forced to supply 5,000 yuan and 200 guns. The president of the Chamber of Commerce could not provide it and was also kidnapped. They occupied the area for two days. Dong's local defense troops from Yuxian were ordered to take the north of Laiyuan directly. Li's regiment of Feng Zhian's division of the 29th Army came to help from Dingxian, dividing their troops to take Wulongkou, Jinshuikou, and Huang'anling to cut off the bandits' route south. Gao's regiment of the Jin army left Lingqiu to attack the west of Laiyuan. On the afternoon of the 9th, the telephone and telegraph lines of Laiyuan, Quyang, Yixian, Wanxian, and Tangxian were destroyed by bandits, and news could not get through. There was a great shock. The local defense forces of each county were all transferred to the border to guard it. Villagers from each county fled in droves. On the night of the 9th, the bandits learned that the government army was attacking in three directions, and they abandoned the city in a panic, fleeing through the borders of Yixian and Laiyuan counties, crossing villages such as Caicungang, Chajianling, and Shizhuangpu, looting along the way. At 11 a.m. on the 10th, they had fled to Zoumayi, posing a threat to Anxin in the south via Tangxian and Wanxian counties. The Second Regiment of the 53rd Army arrived in Tangxian in the afternoon of the 10th to block the bandits from fleeing south. Li's regiment of the 29th Army followed closely behind the bandits. As of the afternoon of the 11th, the bandits were divided into infantry and cavalry, some fleeing towards Yixian and Tangxian counties, and some fleeing towards Wanxian and Anxin counties. The counties in the heart of Hebei Province were in a panic due to the approaching end of the year. The counties telegraphed the province one after another, asking to send troops to block them quickly. However, since the 29th Army was transferred to garrison and the 32nd Army was sent south, and most of the 53rd Army was also transferred to Shaanxi and Gansu to undertake bandit suppression work, the province was so vast that the military strength was actually insufficient. Therefore, Bandit Liu's decision to lead his troops to flee east and west has left the defenses of each county empty. Although the troops have been mobilized to intercept them, opportunities have been repeatedly lost, resulting in the failure to completely eliminate them. Furthermore, the bandit gang has a significant background and is supplied with guns and ammunition, with heavy weapons to confront the government army, so the disaster is even worse than in the past. (13th)

Shortage of Subsidiary Currency in Guangdong Province: Retail Trade Greatly Affected; Authorities Begin to Recast Copper Coins 63

Guangzhou Dispatch: After Guangdong Province abolished the use of silver fractional currency and implemented legal tender, legal tender has circulated without obstruction. However, the market suddenly lacked several tens of millions of two-jiao silver coins, which caused great inconvenience to trade. The authorities have rushed to print five-mao and two-mao fractional notes for issuance. However, each issuance is only two to three hundred thousand yuan, and small transactions in society are still extremely difficult. Furthermore, unscrupulous merchants seized the opportunity to buy up these small fractional notes, manipulating them for profit. Therefore, small fractional notes on the market are becoming increasingly scarce. As a result, one yuan of legal tender is only equivalent to nine jiao of small fractional notes. Consumers are, in effect, suffering losses, while stores are reducing their business due to a lack of small fractional coins for change. At the same time, hawkers are adopting a tightening policy due to the rising prices of fractional notes and copper coins, and the business of hawkers has become bleak. Therefore, at this urgent and challenging time of year, Guangdong Province's finances have suddenly presented a tight shortage.

The financial authorities, in order to alleviate the panic of small subsidiary currency, have recently started to mint new-style copper coins for uniform use, divided into one-fen and half-fen denominations. Ten one-fen coins are equivalent to one jiao, and twenty half-fen coins are equivalent to one jiao. The Department of Finance will set up an office to buy old copper coins and recast them. The fineness of the copper coins is said to be 95% bronze and 5% zinc-lead. An initial 4 million coins will be minted for circulation. As for the design of the new copper coins, the front will be engraved with Sun Yat-sen's image, and the back will be printed with the year of manufacture and the denomination. The Department of Finance has dispatched personnel to the mint to repair the factory buildings and repair the coin-minting machines. It is expected that a trial run can be carried out at the end of this month. If it goes smoothly, large-scale minting can officially begin in the middle of next month. In order to save the treasury and utilize waste, in addition to the copper that must be purchased, the military agencies plan to allocate the copper shells of bullets stored for bronze smelting. After this news came out, speculators are now rushing to buy old copper coins to hoard them, so the price of old copper coins on the market has suddenly risen. In the past, one jiao could be exchanged for 32 coins, but soon only 24 coins could be exchanged. Recently, only 20 coins can be exchanged. However, daily commodity prices have not fallen due to the high price of copper coins. (January 11th)

Xiaoshan Extension of Legal Tender Exchange Period by Three Months 75

The Xiaoshan County Government received an order from the provincial government stating that at the beginning of the implementation of the new currency policy by the Ministry of Finance, Article 8 of the Measures for Exchanging Legal Tender was required. Article 1 of the measures stipulated that all holders of silver were required to exchange it for legal tender within three months from November 4th of the 24th year of the Republic of China, which was due to expire on February 3rd of this year. Currently, there are still many places where silver and silver coins have not been exchanged for legal tender as scheduled, and many remote areas still lack the circulation of legal tender and urgently need its promotion. Therefore, the deadline should be appropriately extended to benefit merchants and promote its implementation. It is now ordered by the ministry to continue the original deadline from February of this year, which has been reported to the Executive Yuan for record, and to notify all provincial and county governments and relevant authorities to comply. This county has already complied.

Linpu Chamber of Commerce to Organize Separately by Provincial Order 76

The Shaoshan Linpu Town Chamber of Commerce has been jointly organized by shops in Shaoshan and Xiaoshan counties since the Xuan統 years of the late Qing Dynasty, using the name "Shaoshan Linpu Town Chamber of Commerce." In December, the county government asked the county government of this county, on the instructions of the Construction Department, to organize the town's chamber of commerce according to administrative regions, with each county separately organizing its town chamber of commerce. The chamber of commerce believes that separate organization would not only lead to a lack of talent and difficulties in selecting staff, but also limited funding, making it difficult to develop the chamber's affairs. According to the membership list, there are only over 140 shops in the entire town, excluding Zhu Mu, who joined the trade association. Over 100 of these are in Xiaoshan, who can organize on their own, while less than 50 are in Shaoxing, making it impossible to organize independently. Although the town is divided between Shaoshan and Xiaoshan counties, the shops are still close to each other. The reasons for not being able to separate were explained to the county party headquarters, which then forwarded the situation to the provincial and central departments for review. Yesterday, instructions were received from the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters stating that since the laws and regulations have changed, the town's chamber of commerce should be organized separately. Yesterday, the county party headquarters forwarded the order to the town's chamber of commerce for compliance.

Rural Life Talks 77

— Edited by Yu Qingtang

Land Relationships and Agricultural Management in Lingjiaqiao, Hang County - Guo Renquan

The author has been residing in Lingjiaqiao for less than two months. The following narrative consists mostly of scattered facts gleaned by the author from conversations with several local elderly farmers.

(I)

To understand the overview of Lingjiaqiao, one must first talk about the Shangsi District to which Lingjiaqiao belongs. The Shangsi District is located in the southeastern part of Hang County, with half of its district boundary being the bank of the Qiantang River. The entire district is divided into twenty-one townships, plus the town of Zhoujiapu. There are many small mountains rising from the ground within the district, with the mountain area totaling 100,000 mu, accounting for one-third of the total area of the district. The area of paddy fields, on the other hand, is only slightly less than 90,000 mu. Of these 90,000 mu of paddy fields, it is estimated with reasonable certainty that more than 60% are occupied by officials and merchants in the urban area of Hangzhou. Therefore, the 140,000 to 150,000 shi of rice that can be produced from these 90,000 mu of fields can hardly feed the 49,000 farmers in the entire district after deducting 50,000 to 60,000 shi of rent rice. The god of hunger drives these farmers to develop the mountains, and growing tea and planting bamboo become the main secondary occupations of the farmers in this district. The entire district has 26,000 mu of tea mountains and tea land, and over 14,000 mu of bamboo forests. Sericulture and duck farming also play an important role in the livelihood of farm families in some villages in this district. What is particularly noteworthy is duck farming. In Xinlan Township, many forest households simply regard it as their only main business. Most of them live on the sandy beaches along the Qiantang River, living in thatched huts. When you approach their residences, you can hear the sound of "Gha! Gha! Gha!" constantly coming from the thatched sheds from hundreds of paces away.

Lingjiaqiao, a village of about 250 households, is located in the center of a township in the Shangsi District – Dingshan Township. Because of its central location and convenient transportation (the Hangfu Highway passes through here, only forty minutes away from Hangzhou), political and educational institutions such as the supervisor's office, the field tax collection office, the permit issuance office, and the Zhejiang Provincial Experimental Public Education Hall are all located here. At the same time, because there are no larger towns near Lingjiaqiao, there are also several small shops opened here, such as tea houses, pharmacies, barbershops, grocery stores, etc., which do not make it a purely rural village.

(II)

Among the approximately 250 households in the village, one landlord owns 100 mu of land, and five or six larger self-cultivating farmers and landlords each own 30 to 50 mu of land. For the remaining farm families, being able to own and cultivate a few mu of their own fields is considered very fortunate. More than half of the farm families cultivate purely rented fields. Fortunately, most of them have a few mu or fen of hillside land of their own, and as long as the hillside is not covered with uncultivable rocks, they have already cultivated it and planted tea trees. Most of the farm families' expenses depend on the income from selling tea in the spring season. Relying solely on a few mu of rented paddy fields, it is feared that many farm families cannot even maintain their food supply. Therefore, the price of tea is truly the lifeline of the farmers in Lingjiaqiao. The price of tea this spring is worse than in previous years, and it has already posed a considerable threat to the majority of farm families.

The rented fields cultivated by the farmers in Lingjiaqiao, like other villages in the Shangsi District, are mostly owned by officials and merchants in the urban area of Hangzhou. As early as fifty or eighty years ago, those officials and merchants entrusted reliable people to buy in large quantities in this village. "Land is the property of descendants for all generations." The officials and merchants all had such an understanding, investing their extorted wealth in the countryside, planting a solid, lasting network of bloodsucking. They spent scarce silver (only about ten yuan per mu), but received a continuous supply of white rice over the years. Precisely because their purpose was "white rice," they often did not pay attention to the location and quality of the fields when they bought them. Some farmers, because they were too poor, hoped to get a higher price for their fields and even sold three mu as four mu. The buyers only needed to receive the rent rice for four mu, so why bother asking about the actual size of the field?

Rent collectors want rent rice. As long as these tenant farmers do not owe rent rice, they can enjoy the right to cultivate permanently. The author has visited many farmers and asked them about the term of their tenancy for a certain paddy field. Their answers were often: "It was the ancestral property sold by our grandfather, and we have been cultivating it for sixty or seventy years." This de facto permanent cultivation has not formed the so-called perpetual tenancy. The farmers here have never heard of terms such as "Min Ke Tian" (people's guest land) or "Da Xiao Mai" (big and small sale). When they are too poor to pay the rent rice, they can only watch their paddy fields being cultivated by others. They often panic: What will happen if we can't pay the rent, and the tenancy is revoked?

The rent for the urban landlords' fields is fixed, ranging from five dou to one shi per mu, with six dou to eight dou being common. The 25% rent reduction is generally implemented here. Before the 16th year of the Republic, rent was collected as is. From the 16th to 18th years of the Republic, rent was paid at 37.5% of the estimated total harvest. From the 19th year of the Republic, the method of estimating the total harvest was abolished, and rent was paid at a 25% discount on the original rent amount for each rented field.

One landlord and five or six wealthy farmers in this village also rent out a total of 170 to 180 mu of land to the poor farmers in the village. Some small landlords in the village, aware of how urgently the poor farmers in the village need land, therefore collect relatively higher rents, either dividing the harvest at a ratio of 4 (landlord) to 6 (tenant), or setting a fixed rent amount without a 25% rent reduction, because they themselves feel that the burden of field taxes has not been reduced and is continuing to increase.

In the past five years, due to the pressure of grain dumping by international imperialism, grain prices across the country have been falling, which has affected land prices. Lingjiaqiao is no exception. However, the price of tea land has increased in the past five years. This is related to the increase in local tea sales and can be regarded as an exception in this area:

Price per Mu of Paddy Field Price per Mu of Tea Land

Current 5 Years Ago Current 5 Years Ago

Highest 90 Yuan 120 Yuan 90 Yuan 50 Yuan

Average 40 Yuan 80 Yuan 40 Yuan 25 Yuan

Lowest 10 Yuan 40 Yuan 10 Yuan 10 Yuan

Farmers regard tea land as the "rising star" of wealth generation. Despite the rising prices, ordinary farmers rarely sell it. At present, the sale and purchase of paddy fields is more common. With the decline in field prices, the trend of land concentration has not weakened slightly. A merchant in Lingjiaqiao has used the profits from his tea business to buy over thirty mu of fields from the farmers in this village in the past five or six years. Large landlords in the city, aware of the rising tide of farmer movements and the reduction of rents, want to sell their land, but in this day and age, hoping that farmers will buy the land is just a dream. Therefore, the landlord's attitude of regarding their land as worthless does not immediately reduce the seriousness of the land problem. (To be continued)

Rumors of Public Debt Interest Rate Reduction and Postponement Spread Widely. Minister Kong Calls for Meeting with Financial Circles. General Manager Qian Xinzhi of the Four Banks Goes to Beijing to Meet Wu and Chen. Securities Trading as Usual Today, Regular Closure Tomorrow. 78

Xinsheng News Agency reports that after the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and other organizations telegraphed the government to protect credit, Yu Zuoting, Jin Runyang, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, and others were summoned to Beijing by telegram from the Executive Yuan to inquire in person. After returning to Shanghai, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi called a meeting with leaders of the financial community the night before last. Qian Xinzhi, Deputy General Manager of the Four Banks Savings Association, went to Beijing the night before last. The Huashang Securities Exchange will open as usual today, with a regular closure from tomorrow onwards for the general closing period. Details are as follows:

Rumors of Interest Rate Reduction and Postponement

Since the Shanghai Incident, former Finance Minister Song Ziwen had consulted with holders of domestic bonds and agreed to slightly reduce the interest rate on the bonds and slightly postpone the repayment date to prevent the depletion of social finance. The National Government ordered the implementation on February 24th of the 21st year of the Republic of China. At that time, the monthly principal repayment fund for the bonds issued by the government was reduced from a total of 18 million yuan to 8.6 million yuan. Since its implementation, the monthly principal repayment fund has exceeded the previously stipulated amount due to the government's increased issuance of financial, customs, Yuping, and telecommunications bonds, totaling 11 million yuan. Recently, after rumors of the government reducing interest rates and postponing the repayment date of bonds spread in the market, all sectors attached great importance to them. Leaders of various organizations, such as the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the financial community, and the Citizens' Federation, telegraphed the government one after another to protect bond credit. At the same time, Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and others were summoned to Beijing by telegram from the Executive Yuan to inquire in person. Although they have returned to Shanghai, securities trading on the Huashang Securities Exchange continues to plummet due to the unabated rumors in the market.

Verbatim Record of the Government Order of the 21st Year of the Republic of China

A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency verbatim recorded the order of the National Government on June 24th of the 21st year of the Republic of China as follows: "Since the Liaoning Incident, the prices of various bonds have plummeted as a result, and the national finances and social economy have suffered. The government has never been late in repaying principal and paying interest. When the Shanghai Incident followed, the bond market suddenly lost its liquidity, and finance was also stagnant. The government and the people are one, sharing weal and woe. At this time of national crisis and financial difficulties, rather than letting the bond market drift, it is better to slightly reduce interest rates and slightly postpone the repayment date to prevent the depletion of social finance. The financial resources to resist aggression can be slightly improved. Repeatedly decorate the example and re-propose appropriate standards. It has also been decided that 8.6 million yuan will be allocated from customs duties each month as a fund for allocating various bonds. The interest rate is 6% per annum, and the repayment period will be handled in accordance with the schedule drawn up by the Ministry of Finance. The relevant revenue officials and the General Tax Office of the Ministry of Finance shall be ordered to transfer the principal and interest of the various bonds in full and on schedule each month until the principal and interest are fully repaid, without any delay. This is the government's most decisive decision to maintain integrity and regulate finance with the people. Once the order is issued, it will be a permanent settlement. In the future, no matter how difficult the finances are, the aforementioned funds shall not be moved slightly, and there shall be no further changes to show great trust. This order."

Finance Minister Calls for Meeting with Financial Circles

After Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the morning before last, he convened a meeting with leaders of the financial community at his private residence on West Ahemes Road the night before last, including Song Hanzhang of the Bank of China, Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, Chen Guangfu, General Manager of the Shanghai Bank, Qian Xinzhi, Deputy General Manager of the Four Banks Savings Association, Ye Zhuotang, General Manager of the Siming Bank, and Hu Bijiang, General Manager of the Zhongnan Bank. It is reported that this matter is also related.

Securities Market Opens as Usual

Securities trading on the Huashang Securities Exchange has been consistently plummeting due to the market being filled with rumors of government interest rate reductions and postponements, causing all bonds to fall across the board. The previous day, military cuts and rehabilitation fell to four yuan and trading was suspended. Yesterday was a regular weekly closure. Today, Monday, it will open as usual. Also, because the general closing period for various industries in the 24th year of the Republic of China has arrived, it has been decided that from tomorrow (the 21st), the market will be closed in accordance with previous years' practices until the general closing is over.

Central News Agency reports that the Central Mint has been ordered to mint decimal subsidiary coins. After the regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan, the mint is now casting two types: copper one fen and nickel five fen. The front features a profile portrait of the Premier, inscribed with the words "Made in the 25th Year of the Republic of China." Its size is similar to the previous single silver hao.

Silk Factories Completely Shut Down. Workers Cling to Old Habits and Return Home for the New Year. Various Silk Merchants All Earned Huge Profits Last Year. 86

After the overseas sales of Chinese silk improved, prices soared, and exports increased significantly. Silk merchants from various factories all earned huge profits. However, due to the lack of raw materials, silk factories in Shanghai, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang were forced to shut down one after another. They will resume operation after the spring cocoons are on the market. Silk factories in Shanghai have temporarily shut down due to the arrival of the general closing period for various industries in the 24th year and the silk reeling workers clinging to their old habits and returning home for the New Year. For example, Fulunheng Shuanggong Factory and others on Tianbao Road have already shut down yesterday and will resume operation after the 27th of this month. However, it is expected that all silk factories will inevitably stop operating due to the lack of raw materials to reel when the spring cocoons are about to be on the market.

Industry Ministry's Silk Relief Plan: Three Major Initiatives Proposed 87

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, the United States has traditionally been the largest importer of Chinese silk, with exports to the U.S. reaching over 30 million yuan last year. France and England are second, but in recent years, due to the dumping of artificial silk by Japan and Italy, the position of Chinese silk has plummeted. Last year, after the "International Raw Silk Trade Conference," uniform standards of quality and pricing were implemented under the repeated supervision of the authorities, finally gaining the trust of foreign merchants. Now, to facilitate sales, the Ministry of Industry has planned to establish Chinese raw silk promotion offices in New York, Paris, Marseille, and London. These offices are expected to be operational by the summer of this year.

Improving Silkworm Breeds: The Ministry of Industry believes that in addition to dumping, poor silk quality is a major factor affecting silk exports. Therefore, this year, it has decided to work with the National Economic Council and the Silkworm Breed Improvement Committee to actively improve silkworm breeds. Zhejiang and Jiangsu provinces have already started their own programs. It is expected that preparations will be completed by March and the improved breeds will be distributed to various counties for application. In addition, silkworm breeds will be purchased from foreign countries. It is reported that the Silkworm Association has confirmed the improvement of 1.5 million sheets of improved silkworm eggs, and currently has 2 million sheets.

Standardizing Brands: Last year, raw silk prices rose sharply abroad, resulting in considerable profits for silk mills. However, there were occasional factory shutdowns, with some mills deliberately halting production. It is estimated that there are currently over 80,000 bales of silk in storage, which can sustain production until the new silkworms come on the market. According to research by the Ministry of Industry, the failure of Chinese silk has many causes, but the lack of standardized brands and pricing is the most detrimental factor. Recently, old-style silk mills in Shanghai, Wuxi, Hangzhou and other cities have machinery that is three or four decades old. If these are not urgently improved, they will be eliminated by the times. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry suggests that factories use their profits to purchase new machinery, working together to overcome the challenges facing the silk industry.

Using National Goods

Executive Yuan Orders City Government to Strictly Prohibit the Collection and Transport of Silver Coins and Silver Items: City Government Has Instructed Subordinate Military Police to Comply 95

The Executive Yuan yesterday ordered the city government, stating: "The currency reform is purely to prevent the outflow of silver, stabilize the financial market, and regulate social capital. However, according to confidential reports, there are many unscrupulous individuals in various places who are raising prices to buy silver coins and silver items, attempting to smuggle them out of the country for profit. Their means of private transactions and smuggling include secretly buying in special areas, or throwing silver packages into the river after the ship has departed, and then retrieving them when the ship sails. They carry them for export, using all kinds of malicious schemes. These unscrupulous individuals only seek profit and disregard the overall situation, which is extremely hateful. Strict investigation and arrest should be carried out immediately, and the full force of the law should be applied to punish them, in order to deter the wicked and safeguard the foundation of the country. You are instructed to inform all subordinate political, military, and police agencies to strictly arrest these individuals. Upon successful capture, they should be immediately sent to the court for strict punishment, without any negligence." It is reported that after receiving the order, the city government has instructed subordinate military and police agencies to comply.

French Ambassador to China, Mr. Naggiar, Expected to Arrive in Mid-February 97

Mr. Naggiar entered the French diplomatic service in 1908. In 1925, he served as the French Consul-General in Shanghai, and was subsequently transferred back to France. Mr. Naggiar is currently 54 years old and lived in China for many years. Shanghai Public Security Bureau Continues Factory Fire Inspections 100

Extended Inspection in the South Shanghai District; Inspections to be Held in Zhabei, West Shanghai, and Pudong

According to the New Sound News Agency, factory fire prevention and the safety of each factory are extremely important. The municipal authorities have always paid attention to this. In order to further improve the fire prevention equipment of various factories, the Municipal Public Security Bureau began inspection work in July last year, dispatching personnel to actively inspect each factory. If improvements were urgently needed, the factories were immediately ordered to correct them, install fire extinguishers, and provide instructions to avoid fire hazards. Since its implementation, the results have been very remarkable. The work is carried out by district. The inspection in the South Shanghai District has been going on for a long time. However, because there are many areas that need to be improved in the various factories, it has been extended slightly and inspections continue, with the aim of ensuring that all factories can make corrections voluntarily. According to the person in charge of the Fire Prevention Section of the Bureau, after the inspection in the South Shanghai District is completed, the three districts of Zhabei, West Shanghai, and Pudong will continue to start at a later date. The inspection date for each district has not yet been determined, and will depend on the results of the inspection. The Bureau believes that factory fire prevention is related to the happiness of all workers in the city, and is also closely related to public safety. Therefore, the inspection cannot be carried out carelessly, and the date must be extended slightly.

Salary Cuts for Staff of Various Bureaus Due to Municipal Government's Austerity Measures 101

According to the Shanghai News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Government has been experiencing empty coffers and a budget deficit in recent years. Therefore, starting in December of the 24th year, the regular expenses of all subordinate agencies have been paid at 80% of the original amount. Now, various bureaus are implementing major austerity measures, including layoffs and salary cuts. Except for staff with salaries below 50 yuan, who are exempt from the discount, all bureaus issue salaries at 80% to 90% of the original amount. The Social Affairs Bureau has larger expenses, so the salaries of its staff have already been discounted by 5% since July of last year, and have been further reduced since December, resulting in a significant shortfall. Therefore, it is proposed that the salaries of staff be uniformly paid at 76% of the original amount. However, low-level staff with salaries below 50 yuan have difficult lives and are at risk of going hungry if their salaries are discounted. Therefore, Director Wu, out of consideration, has decided to find ways to maintain their original salaries.

Most have been completely taken over. Currently, only temporary takeover events, such as old banknotes sent by branch offices in other locations, require the relevant bank to be notified by telephone to go and accept them. As for the Farmers Bank of China, which was originally taken over by the Bank of China, it has now been taken over by the Central Bank.

Jianghai Steamers to Take Holiday Break During Winter Vacation 114

During this cold holiday season at the end of the lunar year, the Jianghai merchant ships in Shanghai will also suspend operations. The following is a list of the companies and routes:

Shanghai-Ningbo Route: China Merchants has been the largest operator on the Shanghai-Ningbo route last year, with 160,000 shipments of cargo and 300,000 passengers. Sanbei also had more than 120,000 yuan due to the large amount of traffic to Zhenhai Port. Taigu and others have decided to allocate the money to Sanbei, but they will all contribute to it this year. During the winter vacation, Taigu's New Beijing will suspend operations after departing from Shanghai on the 22nd. Sanbei's Ningxing will be the last service on the 23rd, docking in Ningbo. It will open to Shanghai on the 27th. Xinjiangtian is a state-run ship and Ning Shao is still operating on schedule.

Tongyang Route: The Tongyang route had an excellent year last year, and Dada and Datong both made a profit. Due to the customs of the winter vacation, it has been decided to suspend operations at the same time from the 22nd, a total of six days from the 28th to February 2nd. During these five days, the two companies agreed to run one ship per day, and the original state will be restored from the 3rd.

Chongsha Route: The Shanghai-Chongming Beisha Route is now also united. There has always been a ship running every day. Now, the companies have agreed to suspend operations uniformly for three days from the 23rd to rest. The small inland river ferries, such as the Huzhou route, will also suspend operations for three days starting from the 23rd.

Jianghai Vessels: The six Yangtze River shipping companies will suspend operations for two days as in previous years, namely the 24th and 25th. Sanbei's Xin Ningxing was ordered to come early from Hankou so that it could arrive in Shanghai one day earlier to rest. The North and South Ocean routes are not operating because they cannot be assigned to schedule and there is a shortage of goods and passengers during the winter vacation. They will not be able to resume operations until after the 26th.

Slaughtering Industry Stops Taking Piglets from Nanshi Trade Warehouses Yesterday: Fresh Pig Vendors Association Petitions Party Headquarters for Relief 116

According to the East China News Agency, the Shanghai Fresh Pig Slaughtering Industry Association is complaining that the Nanshi pig trade warehouses are collecting piglets for slaughter and that workers are forcibly plucking pig bristles. Several negotiations have been ineffective, so they have stopped taking piglets for slaughter from the Nanshi warehouses starting yesterday. The details are as follows:

Slaughtering Industry Stops Taking Slaughtered Pigs

A total of 24 slaughtering companies in the Nanshi area have all stopped taking slaughtered piglets from Nanshi pig trade warehouses starting yesterday. The counterparts in the concession areas were informed too late, so they are still taking goods from Nanshi. It is estimated that they will all stop taking goods today. The counterparts of the association in Zhabei take goods from Wusong, because the fresh pig industry in Wusong is well managed and there is no malpractice of forcibly plucking pig bristles.

Vendors Association Petitions for Relief

After the slaughtering industry stopped taking goods, the Fresh Pig Trade Association and the Fresh Meat Industry Association have not yet made any statements. The Fresh Pig Vendor Association, on the other hand, believes that the losses suffered by each counterpart are huge and has begun to panic. The association has petitioned the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for relief and sent representatives to negotiate with the Fresh Pig Trade Association at 5 pm yesterday in order to resolve the issue immediately.

Jiangnan Chemical Industrial Plant Creates Domestically Produced Bleaching Powder, Capital Increase of 100,000 Yuan Fully Subscribed 117

The Jiangnan Chemical Industrial Plant, located on Gonghe Xin Road in Zhabei, was the first acetic acid plant in the East. It was established in 1933 by Xu Shixing and Ge Guiye, using wood as raw material. By 1934, it was fully operational, producing high-quality products that were favored by many domestic factories. However, production was too small to meet demand. Leading merchants such as Shen Zhongyi, Zhang Rongchu, Zhu Luquan, Fei Liangsheng, Zhou Lianbu, and Zhao Shichun invested to expand and reorganize the plant. Dr. Xue Jimin was hired as the chief engineer. Xue, with his ingenuity, built four dry distillation stoves himself. Other equipment, such as tar machines, wood alcohol machines, and drying machines, were also designed and built in-house, achieving remarkable results. Each day, 400 dan of firewood were used to produce over 3,000 pounds of high-quality acetic acid. The plant also produced many by-products, such as carbolic acid, turpentine, refined wood alcohol, and medicine for lung diseases. The raw materials were only three: firewood, lime, and sulfuric acid, making it a purely domestic product. Recently, Dr. Xue, after further research, discovered that adding salt would produce high-quality bleaching powder. The required equipment, in addition to the existing generator, only needed new-style electrolytic cells. This would be highly efficient, achieving two goals at once. The plant authorities have already ordered various necessary machines from famous European and American factories. The new project is expected to be completed between May and June, and production will begin then. A decision was also made to increase capital by 100,000 yuan to strengthen the plant's financial position. The shares were subscribed by the shareholders, and it is said that the full amount has been raised. This is truly good news for China's industrial sector.

National Labor Bureau's China Branch Releases Report on the Situation of Overseas Chinese in Vladivostok; There Are Currently Over 23,000 Overseas Chinese, Mostly Laborers Living in Difficult Conditions 121

Riri News reports that yesterday, the China branch of the International Labor Bureau released a report on the situation of overseas Chinese in Vladivostok. According to a survey by the local consulate general: The Soviet government has no immigration regulations and treats overseas Chinese equally with its own citizens, with no special provisions. There are a total of 23,800 overseas Chinese in Vladivostok city and the coastal Ussuri region under the consulate's jurisdiction. Since the Soviet Union implemented state-owned industries and commerce, all foreign businesses have been completely eliminated. Therefore, with the exception of a few property owners and property agents, all overseas Chinese in the Soviet Union are laborers. They work eight or seven hours a day, with one day off every six days. Their monthly income ranges from 100 to 300 rubles, while their monthly expenses range from 150 to 250 rubles. The cost of living in the area is high. Only those with skills have higher incomes and can barely manage. Most others have difficulty making ends meet, and their lives are difficult. Furthermore, Soviet law prohibits the export of domestic currency. Therefore, the income earned by foreigners can only be used within the Soviet Union and cannot be remitted to support families. When leaving the Soviet Union to return home, they cannot take the currency with them.

The Bank of Communications' Trust Deposit Business is Booming; Deposits Since Opening Total 2.5 Million Yuan 123

The Bank of Communications allocated a fund of 2.5 million yuan in national currency as the foundation for its trust department. Since starting the trust deposit business on January 10th, it has offered ordinary trust deposits (opening accounts with 50 yuan or more, a one-year term, seven days' notice required for withdrawal, interest up to 6.5%, with all interest up to that percentage going to the depositor, and any interest exceeding 6.5% being split, with the bank taking half as a trust fee and the rest going to the depositor) and special trust deposits (minimum deposit of 5,000 yuan per account, term and usage determined by the depositor, with the bank deducting a trust fee and the rest going to the depositor). The business has been very successful. Since opening, the total amount of deposits has exceeded 500,000 yuan, with ordinary trust deposits being the most popular. Now, the bank, in response to depositor requests, has decided to issue passbooks for ordinary trust deposits, allowing depositors to deposit money at any time.

Thoroughly Planning Relief for Vagrant Beggars; Public Security Bureau to Begin Implementation Immediately; Immediate Arrest and Separate Accommodation; Those Willing to Return Home Will Be Helped to Do So 124

In order to maintain public order and provide relief to vagrant beggars in the city, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has drafted a plan to thoroughly address the issue and will begin implementation immediately. Details are as follows:

Measures to Provide Rescue and Steps to Take

The Municipal Public Security Bureau recognizes that due to the natural and man-made disasters of the past year, rural areas have become bankrupt, the economy has declined, and many refugees have been unable to make a living, resulting in a large influx of refugees into Shanghai. Shanghai is a mixed Chinese and foreign settlement, with a dense population, developed transportation, and public order that must be maintained. Many refugees, after arriving in Shanghai, gather at wharves and train stations, stealing travelers' belongings to make a living, or engage in illegal and criminal activities throughout the city. In order to maintain public order and thoroughly provide relief, the bureau has decided to implement a beggar relief plan, to be carried out in January, February, and March, with the head of the relief division, Yin Guanzhi, responsible for overseeing everything. According to the division head, speaking to a reporter from Xin Sheng News, the plan has been approved by Director Cai and will begin implementation soon. The steps to be taken are as follows: In January, consult with various charitable organizations to discuss relief measures and issue orders to subordinates to implement the regulations. In February, investigate the number of people receiving relief and conduct inspections at important locations. In March, continue to investigate the number of people receiving relief and conduct inspections at important locations, and compile statistics.

Decisions Made and Implementation to Begin Immediately

The bureau has decided on a comprehensive relief plan for vagrant beggars, as follows: Consult with various charitable organizations in the city (such as the Hubei Nanbihan Shelter, the Unemployed Training Center, the Civilian Education Center, and the Women's Temperance Association, etc.) to discuss effective ways to provide relief to vagrant beggars and establish close cooperation. Issue orders to subordinates to begin arresting beggars immediately. Male beggars should be sent to the Hubei Nanbihan Shelter, while female beggars should be sent to the Women's Temperance Association for education. Those who voluntarily wish to return home, regardless of gender, should be reported to the bureau at any time, which will consult with charitable organizations to arrange their return to their hometowns. Beggars with extremely poor character who are deemed irredeemable may be sent to the Unemployed Training Center or the Civilian Education Center for compulsory accommodation and education. Personnel will be dispatched at any time to inspect important transportation locations.

Recent News from the Lixin Accounting Tutorial School 126

The Lixin Accounting Tutorial School, located at 190 Ningbo Road, was founded by accountant Dr. Pan Xulun. It has been in operation for eight years. Originally, it had two departments: correspondence courses and night school. The correspondence courses can be started at any time, while the night school enrolls students twice a year, in the spring and autumn. Over the years, the school has graduated over 5,000 students. It is reported that the 16th class had over 450 students. The current semester is ending, and preparations are underway to wrap it up. The 17th class is scheduled to begin on February 3rd, and registration is open now. The classes offered are divided into elementary and advanced levels. The elementary level offers the following courses: Elementary Bookkeeping, Advanced Bookkeeping (Chinese and English), Commercial Arithmetic, and Abacus. The advanced level offers the following courses: Advanced Accounting, Corporate Accounting, Bank Accounting, Government Accounting, Accounting Mathematics, Cost Accounting, and Auditing. To make it easier for students in the Nanshi area to study, the school continues to operate a branch school at 25 Xuexi Street, Wenchao Road, Ximen, Nanshi. It has recently been reported that since the school started enrolling students, registration for various courses has been very enthusiastic.

The Dredging Bureau Announces High Tide on Lunar New Year's Day; Due to the Moon's Proximity to Earth; The Magnitude Will Be the Greatest of the Winter 128

According to the prediction of the Hydrology Department of the Dredging Bureau, there will be a high tide in the Huangpu River on the 24th (Lunar New Year's Day). This is because the date coincides with the full moon, and three days later, the moon will be closest to Earth. The resulting magnitude will be the greatest of the winter. The predicted time and magnitude of the high tide are as follows: The high tide on the 24th will begin to rise from 11:05 AM. At 12:05 PM, the rise will suddenly become more rapid, with a water flow rate of 1.8 nautical miles per hour. By 1:00 PM, it will have reached its highest point, with a predicted magnitude of 10 feet 3.5 inches. The ebb tide will begin at 3:25 PM and will be completely receded by 10:00 PM.

Child's Head Found on Henry Road; Contained in a Rush Bag; The Body is Missing 130

At 2:30 AM yesterday, a detective from the French Concession Foch Police Station, number 103, was on patrol when he discovered an abandoned rush bag by the side of the road in front of number 12 Henry Road. The bag was neatly wrapped, arousing suspicion. The detective immediately went forward, untied the bag, and opened it for inspection. To his shock, he found a child's head inside. He was terrified and immediately reported it to the Foch Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. It seemed that the child had died of illness and was then decapitated. Judging by the child's appearance, he/she was less than one year old, only a few months old. There were slight traces of blood where the head was cut off. The gender could not be determined, but the body was nowhere to be found, and it was unknown where it had been buried or discarded. Today, the matter will be reported to the Second Special District Court for officials to conduct an examination. Meanwhile, the police station has ordered all detectives to investigate and arrest the person who abandoned the body and bring them to justice. According to general speculation, the parents of the deceased child believed that the child would not grow up and was a "debt-collecting ghost." Hence, they resorted to this cruel measure to prevent the dead ghost from being reborn in the future, so that subsequent children could grow up safely. This superstitious act is truly ridiculous.

The entire building is constructed with cement and steel, and is well-lit and well-ventilated. Sanitation equipment is currently being installed. The hall's various machines, including 33 types of weaving machines, 30 types of spinning machines, more than 10 air conditioning machines, and other experimental equipment, have all been delivered to the hall and are currently being installed under the guidance of engineers. The original letter is transcribed as follows: "Respected Sirs, Sanxian Lake is a prosperous town in Nanxian, located in the fourth district of Nanxian. The fourth district consists of more than thirty settlements, including Tiancheng, Jixian, and Laoyan, and is the largest area in the entire county. In the 20th year of the Republic of China [1931], it suffered an unprecedented flood, with everything submerged. In the 21st, 22nd, and 23rd years [1932-1934], although the main embankment did not collapse, those within the courtyard that collapsed and produced nothing accounted for nearly one-third. Unexpectedly, in the 24th year [1935], there was again continuous spring rain, and continuous summer rain. The Xiang, Zi, Huan, and Feng rivers simultaneously burst, reaching a water level one foot higher than in the 20th year, turning everything into a watery land. Pitiful farmers, many of whom drowned. Homes, agricultural tools, etc., were all washed away. The embankments are in danger with the sound of crying filling the air. Although the disaster situation is severe, the Hunan government has provided emergency relief by distributing porridge and providing funds to send the disaster victims away. Due to the severity of the disaster and the shortage of funds, the relief work was soon suspended. Temporary work loans were also issued, and late rice and miscellaneous grains were planted. However, due to the autumn flood, the water submerged and the wind destroyed them. High-field white rice accounted for the majority, with very little harvest. Low-lying fields were completely submerged, and the even lower fields are still submerged to this day. In this harsh winter, with ice and snow everywhere, the wailing disaster victims are fighting for nameless vegetable leaves to barely survive. Some are suffering from hunger and cold, and are on the verge of starvation. Some are displaced and their whereabouts are unknown. The misery of these disaster victims is beyond words. If we do not seek urgent relief, starvation is inevitable. Therefore, we are making a special report on the disaster situation and earnestly requesting that personnel be dispatched to conduct an on-site survey and widely distribute disaster relief funds to save the disaster victims."
