Chen Kaiqing's Rough Stone Case: Appeal to the Administrative Court Based on the Principle of Not Punishing Twice for the Same Offense 148

Request to revoke the original confiscation order. The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that Fujianese merchant Chen Kaiqing, due to the rough stones he was transporting being deemed underpriced by the Jianghai Customs, was fined after a separate valuation. While the stones were being processed, they were again seized and confiscated by the Jianghai Customs. The merchant, based on the principle of not punishing twice for the same offense, raised an objection according to Article 31 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations. This objection was overruled by the Penalty Review Committee, which upheld the original order. The merchant, feeling that being punished twice for the same offense was unacceptable, filed an appeal to the Administrative Court according to Article 32 of the Anti-Smuggling Regulations. The statement of appeal is as follows: (A) Facts and History of the Case:

Payment of Tax and Fine: The plaintiff, on April 22nd of this year, transported a piece of rough stone from Burma. He declared the original price to the Jianghai Customs and submitted all relevant documents for inspection (in addition to invoices and other documents, there was also a tax receipt from Burma, which is referred to as the tax bill in this case). The Customs deemed all documents submitted by the plaintiff unreliable and independently valued the stone at 2,000 Rupees, equivalent to 1,234.58 Gold Standard Units. They then considered this a violation of customs regulations (specifically Article 22 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations) and ordered the plaintiff to pay a fine of 600 National Currency Units in addition to the tax based on the assessed value. At the time, the plaintiff was eager to take delivery of the goods for sale and immediately paid the full amount, holding receipts for both the tax and the fine issued by the Customs. He then took possession of the stone.

Circumstances of the Second Seizure: Later, the stone was taken for trial processing in order to sell it at a good price. Unexpectedly, upon trial processing, it was found that the quality of the materials inside was quite excellent, and therefore the plaintiff was unwilling to sell it cheaply. This aroused the jealousy of competitors, and a person named Lu Zhongyi falsely accused the plaintiff to the Customs, resulting in the Customs repossessing and detaining the stone on May 22nd. Despite explanations of the tax payment and fine, the Customs ignored them. At that time, the Customs did not follow the legal procedures and illegally took the stone away without authorization. The plaintiff, fearing the authority, did nothing about it.

Negotiations and Penalties: Subsequently, the plaintiff repeatedly went to the Customs to negotiate, only obtaining a receipt for the detained goods. He repeatedly requested its return, but was told that he must first admit his mistake (without specifying how to admit it). The plaintiff, considering his previous penalty, was unwilling to do so, leading to a stalemate. Seeing that they were unreasonable, the plaintiff repeatedly explained the facts and reasons to the Inspector General of Customs and the Directorate General of Customs, repeatedly requesting legal intervention, but to no avail. Finally, on June 18th of this year, the Inspector General of Customs sent a letter stating that the case was under investigation. Believing that the case was simple and did not require investigation, and fearing that this was a tactic to delay the matter, the plaintiff immediately raised an objection, but it was ignored. On July 18th, another letter from the Inspector General of Customs stated that the case had been submitted to the Directorate General of Customs for review, but no instructions were received from the Directorate General of Customs. Knowing that he was powerless, the plaintiff entrusted the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to forward the matter with a factual account, but there was no reply. It was not until October 3rd that a letter was received from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, enclosing a copy of the Inspector General of Customs' document No. 7935, in which the Customs stated how the plaintiff had committed fraud, etc. While the plaintiff was still astonished, on October 8th, the Customs personally delivered a penalty order, which stated the penalties:

* A fine of 15,000 National Currency Units.

* The jade stone is confiscated, but the owner is allowed to repurchase it at an assessed value of 50,000 Yuan.

* Supplementary import tax is to be paid according to the assessed value of 50,000 Yuan. The reasons for the alleged violation of customs regulations were only the eight characters "submitted fake documents, underreported value," which is exactly the same as the content in Article 22 of the Anti-Smuggling Regulations and the same as the previous penalty.

Review and Decision: The plaintiff, feeling that the reasons given in the order were brief and lacking in detail, making it difficult to defend himself, immediately declared an objection on October 12th in accordance with the law and requested a detailed explanation of the reasons. The reply stated that the penalty in this case had been approved by the Directorate General of Customs, and if the plaintiff was not satisfied, he should file an administrative lawsuit, but the reasons for the penalty were still not explained. Fearing that he would miss the legal deadline, the plaintiff immediately prepared a statement of objection on October 18th, based on the Inspector General of Customs' document No. 7935, and submitted it to the Customs for review. However, on October 21st, the original statement was returned with instructions to proceed as before. The plaintiff, feeling that it was inappropriate to appeal beyond the proper channels, again cited legal examples and submitted it to the Customs for correction, but the Customs remained unenlightened and instead blamed the plaintiff for misunderstanding. At this point, the plaintiff was truly helpless. Just as he was about to file an administrative lawsuit, he suddenly received an order from the Directorate General of Customs on November 1st, pending review by the Penalty Review Committee. At the same time, he received a letter from the Customs asking him to submit additional reasons for the objection. The plaintiff, wanting to resolve the matter quickly, immediately submitted three copies of the prepared statement of objection to the Customs for review the following day. Afterwards, he repeatedly urged them, and after more than a month, on December 12th of this month, he received the decision of the Directorate General of Customs to uphold the original order. Looking at the inconsistencies and illegal actions of the defendants in the procedural aspects of this case, it is truly unbearable for the plaintiff. Therefore, according to Article 32 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations, the plaintiff has filed this lawsuit with your court, requesting relief. (B) Reasons for Disagreeing with the Order and the Decision:

Regarding the order from the first defendant, the Jianghai Customs Tax Office, it only contained the main text and did not provide any reasons, so the plaintiff cannot fathom the reasons for the order and cannot refute them. Here are the points to refute the reasons for the decision of the Penalty Review Committee of the second defendant, the Directorate General of Customs:

Regarding the first item of the review opinions, the principle of "res judicata" (a matter already judged) is a major principle of the rule of law. How can customs penalties be an exception? The provisions of Article 30 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations refer to the subsequent discovery of undeclared goods that have not been penalized beforehand. If a penalty has already been imposed, the provisions of that article do not apply. The original decision intentionally distorts the text, which is outrageous. The decision also states that "the Customs' first decision to punish the merchant was due to underreporting the value of the goods, while the second decision to punish and confiscate the goods was due to the discovery that the tax bill did not belong to the rough stone in this case." This argument is very sophistical. Does the original order not state that the rule violated by the plaintiff was "submitted fake documents, underreported value"? Therefore, the first penalty is for the same reason and the same act as the second penalty and confiscation. This is the first disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the second item of the review opinions, it is stated that "it has long been verified that the tax bill for the rough stone in Burma is taxed at 33.33%, and the tax amount is also clearly stated as 200 Rupees, which can infer that the value of the stone in Burma should be 600 Rupees." It is also stated that "using the tax bill as the valuation standard, the amount stated on it is one-tenth of the price of the stone on board," and "the tax amount of 200 Rupees, multiplied by ten, is 2,000 Rupees, plus the cost of landing and taxes, should be converted to 1,234.58 Gold Standard Units." Based on the above valuation method, anyone would know that it is unreasonable. Saying that it is not based on the tax bill for valuation is certainly credible. It is also stated that "the invoice shows 825 Rupees, which is considered the price on board, so it is equal to the tax bill." If the invoice states this, and the Customs values it like that, then is the submitted invoice not already recognized as fake? That is, there is no need to discuss how to value it, as it has already been considered that there is a situation of submitting fake documents. Why wait until it is discovered that the tax bill does not belong to the rough stone in this case to determine that the plaintiff submitted fake documents? As for the odd amounts, since the Customs themselves stated that it is based on calculation methods, then even if it is odd, it is actually rounded. The terms "one-tenth" and "multiplied by ten" are intended to force a match, but instead expose their own flaws. The committee still forcefully defends it, but where is the so-called "sufficient reason"? This is also disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the third, fourth, and fifth items of the review opinions, according to the principle of "res judicata," even if someone reports, the past situation should be checked first, and then it should be decided whether to accept it or not. One should not rashly detain it, causing unnecessary losses to others. If this example is set, all import merchants in the city will have the risk of having their goods detained at any time, and there will be no peace. Is this the original intention of setting up customs and collecting taxes? The so-called disclosure of the name of the reporter and the reported facts is intended to thoroughly investigate and see the truth of the case. According to the Inspector General of Customs' document No. 7935, it is based on hearsay, Lu Zhongyi's report, described vividly and definitively. After the plaintiff refuted it fully in the statement of reasons for disagreeing with the order, the original decision stated that the Customs' order was not based on this, which clearly shows that the original decision is a castle in the air with no basis. This is the third disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the sixth item of the review opinions, regarding the so-called value problem, the Customs never mentioned the so-called inviting valuation in the original report, only stating that someone came to the Customs for unofficial contact to purchase it. Now, it is said that it is handled according to the regulations, and one of the people is said to be an arbitrary addition. Whether the regulations cited are applicable or whether there was actually a valuation, even if there was, the price estimated in the first decision is absolutely insufficient to be used as a basis, and there is even less reason to say that there is tax evasion and confiscation. Because the thing about rough stones is that before it is trial processed, its appearance is like ordinary rock and has no value. Only after trial processing (commonly known as opening the eye) can a rough estimate be made, and only after complete processing can a more accurate valuation be made. It still needs to be priced by people according to the time after it is processed into utensils. The truth in this is not enough for outsiders to say. Therefore, the valuation after trial processing, even if it is hundreds or thousands of times the original purchase price, or even worthless, is a common occurrence, similar to speculative business. Now, if the second decision estimates the value at 50,000, and in the future it will be 100,000 or 200,000, and then the valuation is followed in sequence, and penalties are imposed in turn, is there such a reason in the world? The committee did not know the truth, but only thought about ordinary things. It is not surprising that their understanding is insufficient, but at the beginning when the stone was detained, the truth was briefly stated to the Directorate General of Customs. Why is it so forgetful? Moreover, the method of appraisal of goods by the public must be done by hiring experts in a public way and must never be done by the Customs in a secretive way. This is the fourth disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the seventh item of the review opinions, whether there is a Baozhen Company mark on the stone is a major question. Since the committee examined it and said that it was clearly visible and obvious to the eye, the plaintiff cannot say that it is certainly not there. But how does the committee know for sure that the rough stone they saw is the rough stone in this case? How do they know for sure that the mark they saw is the actual mark placed by the company? Whether the ink color is new or old, please have an expert appraise it. Also, why was the plaintiff not present at the time of the examination? And the plaintiff has repeatedly requested to see the stone, why was it rejected? All this makes the plaintiff very suspicious. Also, when the Customs detained the stone, they did not follow the legal procedures, neither issuing a formal receipt nor noting the characteristics of the stone on any record. The plaintiff has been touching the stone day and night, and has never seen the Baozhen Company mark. Now the Customs suddenly discovers the mark. Therefore, regarding the authenticity of the mark and whether the mark existed before the detention, the Customs has the responsibility to provide evidence. The plaintiff still has the following points of defense regarding this item:

The stone has been detained for a long time and anything can be done. The stone has been detained at the Customs for more than half a year, and it is easy to add crimes and do whatever they want. The mark on the stone is only a sign for the tax merchant and does not have any external duties, so all use Chinese ink, which can be washed off and will not be permanently preserved. Now the mark they see has not been proven to be the company's true mark, nor has the ink been inspected. And according to the Customs' investigation, the so-called Zhang Bao and others have been dead for several years, so no one can come out to acknowledge it. How do they know that it was not added later? Why did the committee not see this?

Deliberately inspected, but nothing was seen. According to the mark seen by the committee, it is very visible and obvious to the eye. Then, when the Customs inspected and valued it, even after repeated and detailed viewing, why didn't they see it? It is said that recently the rough stones declared to customs all have marks on them. Stones have not started today, and marks have long been seen. And since they have been priced based on the documents for a long time, the relationship between the documents, goods, and stamps should have been well known. Therefore, the inspection at the time was a clear sign of comparison between the documents and goods. How could it not be discovered such a clearly visible mark? Now it suddenly appears, which is strange.

The handling process is incredible. After the stone was detained, the plaintiff went to the Customs to negotiate many times, but the Customs never mentioned the discovery of the mark, nor did they ask the plaintiff to acknowledge it. And according to the original report, because this mark was discovered, the Burmese government was investigated, and the government's reply telegram was received in June. Why couldn't it be announced and judged directly, but had to be reviewed and handled for several months? The actions of the anti-smuggling department are incredible, probably because there is no supporting evidence and they are shirking responsibility.

It is not possible to replace the goods. Rough stone is a natural product and is not man-made. The size and weight are different and cannot be changed. If it is suspected of being replaced, the tax bill clearly lists the weight, about 640 Chinese pounds, which was verified by the Customs at the time of valuation and found to be correct. Since the weight of the stone cannot be changed, how can it be so coincidental to replace it? Now, instead of thinking about this, they discovered a mark and then inquired about it from people thousands of miles away, which is abandoning the near and seeking the far, and the intention is unknown.

There are three marks on one side, which is very strange. There are no rules for tax merchants to stamp, only for easy identification. To be identified, it should be stamped on the front where it is easy to see. Now there are as many as three on the side, and all other parts are completely absent. Instead of stamping the mark on the front, which is convenient for stamping, three are stamped on the side, which is very strange. If all the others have been erased and nothing remains, then why are these three left, and they are very visible? Is it not strange? If the final suspicion is the truth, then it is just a case of overreaching.

It is not difficult to chemically test the age of the ink. The part of the photos taken is extremely small, and it cannot be determined that it is not the rough stone in this case. The marks taken cannot be concluded to be fake. Comparing the other photos attached, the degree of visibility is almost the same. However, the mark stamped ten years ago is as clear as the one recently stamped. Even the most stupid people cannot believe it. Although it is not difficult to test the age of the ink by chemical methods, due to the prestige of the country, no one can but maintain the dignity of the customs and give a fair judgment. The Customs may have seen this, so they rashly made a statement, and they did not dare to ask for an inspection, which is very frightening.

It is easy for the reporters to design and frame them. According to what the plaintiff said, there is more than one reporter, Lu Zhongyi. It is also said that "Lu Zhongyi said in person", "the stone should be carefully observed", "there should be no such mark", etc. Judging from the meaning of this paragraph, although it is not said what day it happened, it can be seen that the reporters come to the Customs from time to time, and the Customs discuss with them. It can also be seen that they are allowed to watch at any time, hoping to find something. If so, it is easy for them to forge the mark and stamp it on the stone, and then make a face-to-face statement. It was discovered on the side of the stone, and it can be inferred that it was done intentionally, so as to avoid not seeing it during the valuation, or to make the Customs believe it. This is the fifth disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the eighth item of the review opinions, the so-called finding the Baozhen mark is a huge injustice, so all the Burmese government's telegrams are the finishing touch. List the known facts reported by Lu Zhongyi, and add words such as "is" and "was" so that the question can be answered, so as to punish. The reason is very clear. It is said that it has nothing to do with this case, which is a light statement. This is the sixth disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the ninth item of the review opinions, the first item of the review opinions and the opinions in the original decision clearly stated that the tax bill does not belong to the rough stone in this case, which means it is replaced. If so, why say it two or three times? This is to fabricate words and make it easy to convict. The original book said that it failed to determine the facts of the whole case, which is true. It is said that it is suspected of its crime, which is also true. The committee defended it, but what is the intention? This is the seventh disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the tenth item of the review opinions, the tax bill is as mentioned above, so let it be. The plaintiff did not consider himself a shareholder of the company, so there should be no possibility of forgery. Also, this invoice has been signed by the consul, so it is impossible to collude. This is the eighth disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the eleventh item of the review opinions, the original book stated that it was just briefly mentioned for fear that outsiders would not understand the truth. If they pay attention to this, then the price estimated in the second decision is not credible. Once the tax is paid and released, it should not be questioned, and there is no need to wait until the future. This is the ninth disagreement with the original decision.

Regarding the twelfth item of the review opinions, Lu Zhongyi's malicious accusation is a narrative of the origin of this case. But why he dared to be so bold is even more difficult to ensure that he has no background. It is okay not to investigate it thoroughly, but it is not the point to say that it has nothing to do with this case. This is the tenth disagreement with the original decision. Looking at the situation of this case, the most important point is whether all the actions of the Customs in handling this case are legal. Secondly, after a penalty has been imposed once, for the same fact, based on the same regulations, and for the same act, can a heavier penalty be added? Secondly, whether submitting fake documents and underreporting the value are related under the circumstances of this case and regarded as the same act. Fourthly, whether the submitted invoice is one of the documents, and the tax bill has been used to estimate the price. Since it has not been believed and a separate price has been estimated, this is not considered submitting fake documents. The last point is whether the so-called invitation to estimate the price actually happened, and whether the regulations cited are applicable. As for the matter of discovering the Baozhen stamp, the plaintiff does not consider it important to this case, and the defendant, as stated above, has not fulfilled his responsibility to provide evidence. The plaintiff cannot admit it even if he dies. Therefore, based on the above reasons, this lawsuit is filed in accordance with the law. I respectfully request that your court, taking into account that the plaintiff is innocent and has suffered misfortune for more than half a year, quickly conduct a fair trial and revoke the original order of the first defendant and the original decision of the second defendant in accordance with the law, and order the defendants to return the rough stone to the plaintiff, in order to uphold justice. I am very much looking forward to your order. Respectfully submitted to the Administrative Court, Petitioner: Chen Kaiqing, December 27th, Year 24.

After the Zhonghua Jiande Association closed down last year, creditors such as Tang Chunshou filed a petition with the Shanghai First Special District Court for bankruptcy. Zhonghua Jiande Association: A case of declaring bankruptcy has been adjudicated by this court. Announcement is hereby given as follows: Main text of the adjudication: The debtor, Zhonghua Jiande Association, shall be bankrupt at 11:00 AM on January 15th, 25th year of the Republic of China.

Name of the bankruptcy administrator: Accountant Li Zheng (office located at 367 Jiangxi Road) is selected as the bankruptcy administrator for this case. Deadline for filing rights: Within two and a half months from the date of declaration of bankruptcy (from January 15th to March 31st, 25th year of the Republic of China), creditors should bring their account books or evidence to declare their claims to the bankruptcy administrator. Date of the first meeting of creditors: February 15th of this year, 1:00 PM, in the auditorium of this court. Debtors in bankruptcy and holders of property belonging to the bankrupt estate shall not pay or deliver their property to the bankrupt and shall immediately return it or notify the bankruptcy administrator. Creditors of the bankrupt shall declare their claims to the bankruptcy administrator within the prescribed period. Those who fail to declare within the time limit shall not be entitled to compensation from the bankrupt estate.

Knitwear Guild Members, Stocking Factory Colleagues Jointly Discuss Price Increases 155

Members of the local Knitwear Industry Guild and colleagues from stocking factories held a joint meeting yesterday. Everyone agreed that the market price of raw materials continued to increase, and the cost increased, so the selling price of various types of socks produced by various factories had to be appropriately increased to maintain operations. It was resolved that starting from the spring season, 20-count and below yarn socks would increase by 10% plus an additional 5%; 32-count and 42-count thread socks would increase by 15% plus an additional 10%; 60-count and above thread socks would increase by 10% plus an additional 10%; silk stockings would increase by 20% plus an additional 10%; artificial silk stockings would increase by 20%; and mixed silk stockings would increase by 20%.

Interpretation of Civil Procedure Published 156

The Interpretation of Civil Procedure of the Republic of China, written by legal scholar Dai Jixian, is compiled based on the new Civil Procedure Law that came into effect on July 1, 1935. The content not only fully explains the meaning of the provisions and laws but also clearly indicates the relevant laws or other laws and regulations cited in the interpretation text, so that readers can understand and apply them comprehensively. It has the thoroughness of a lecture style but without other difficulties. The end of the book is attached with an interpretation of the Implementation Law of Civil Procedure, as well as the full book of the new Civil Procedure Law and the old Civil Procedure Law regulations. Moreover, it has been carefully revised by legal expert Guo Wei. Since its publication, it has been highly praised. The book is in two volumes, priced at 3.6 yuan, with a real price of 20% off, and is sold at the Jiuzhou Bookstore on 4th Ma Road in Shanghai.

Statistics of Crimes in This City Last Week 157

The Municipal Public Security Bureau announced that during the past week, from January 11th to January 17th, a total of 275 criminal cases occurred within the jurisdiction, and a total of 505 male and female criminals were arrested. The breakdown is as follows: six robbery cases, involving seven criminals; ninety-three theft cases, involving one hundred and forty-five criminals; fifty-two assault cases, involving ninety-eight criminals; thirty kidnapping cases, involving fifty criminals; one red pill morphine case, involving twenty criminals; five gambling cases, involving fifty-seven criminals; twelve fraud cases, involving four criminals; three arson cases, involving three criminals; nine counterfeit currency cases, involving twelve criminals; one violation of police regulations case, involving one criminal; and thirty-nine other criminal cases, involving sixty-three criminals. The total is two hundred and seventy-five cases, involving five hundred and five criminals. All of the above-mentioned criminals arrested have been preliminarily tried by the Third Section. Except for one hundred and twenty-eight who were released after being dealt with or sentenced according to the Violation of Police Regulations Law due to minor circumstances, all other criminals have been sent to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. Sanitary Conditions in the Public Concession in December 159

According to the Public Concession Health Department's report for December of last year, the sanitary conditions in the city last month did not undergo any major changes. Except for a few exceptions, all notifiable infectious diseases were not significantly different from the same month of the previous year. Malaria has also sharply decreased due to the weather. An outbreak of diphtheria occurred at a certain Chinese children's school established by the Bureau, but thanks to the effective handling by the newly established school health team, the disease did not spread. Furthermore, due to the inclement weather, vaccination work could not be carried out as much as possible. Therefore, the number of people vaccinated last month was only 25,976. However, several cases of smallpox occurred within the Concession during the month. Those who have not been vaccinated recently should take measures to get vaccinated as soon as possible for prevention, especially the laboring class, which cannot be delayed.

Furthermore, the statistics for births and deaths in the Concession in this city in December show that 83 foreign babies were born, 75 of whom resided within the Concession, including 43 male babies and 32 female babies. The number of Chinese babies born has decreased compared to last month, with only over 1,500 reported, 1,459 of whom resided within the Concession, including 760 male babies and 699 female babies. Regarding deaths, 45 foreigners died, of whom non-Chinese Asians accounted for 58%. The biggest causes of death were tuberculosis, pneumonia, typhoid fever, tumors, and suicide. The biggest causes of death for Chinese were old age, tuberculosis, brain diseases, heart disease, and bronchitis.

Amendments to Transport Regulations for Three Types of Dangerous Drugs 160

The National Federation of Pharmaceutical Industry Associations yesterday sent a letter to the pharmaceutical associations of various cities, stating: Respectfully, in order to facilitate business for colleagues in various regions, our association previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways to amend the general rules for freight car transport and the classification table for dangerous and toxic chemicals, to include drugs such as acetic acid, pyroxylic acid, and liquid ammonia in the list of dangerous goods with a minimum transport quantity of 50 kilograms. We have now received approval No. 3 from the Ministry of Railways, stating: We have noted the submission. After investigation, since acetic acid, pyroxylic acid, and liquid ammonia are essential medical and pharmaceutical products, in order to maintain medical and pharmaceutical supplies, approval is hereby granted to include the above three types of drugs in the list of dangerous quality goods with a minimum transport quantity of 50 kilograms, effective from January 21, 1931. In order to prevent accidents, the packaging methods for the above-mentioned drugs should be conveyed to the pharmaceutical merchants. All shipments must be packed in wooden boxes, and the boxes must be filled with sawdust. In addition to issuing orders to various routes, this approval is hereby issued for notification, and you are requested to notify all parties. This is the approval. Accordingly, it is hereby forwarded to you for your information.

Weather Report 164

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong is sunny and cold, with northwest to northeast winds of varying degrees. The Yangtze River basin and this area are cloudy and cold, with occasional sunshine, with northwest to north light winds of varying degrees. There is fog in the morning. The coastal area south of Ma'an Island is changing from cloudy to overcast, with winter monsoon. Also, within 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 4.9 degrees Celsius, and the lowest was 18.3 degrees Celsius. On the same day last year, the highest was 42.8 degrees Celsius, and the lowest was 21.6 degrees Celsius.

Letter 165

To the Editor,

I recently read a news item in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on January 16, "A Major Fire in Bailianjing, Pudong Last Night," stating that the Yuchang Bamboo Company in Bailianjing Port, Pudong, was a branch of the Hu Yuchang Wood Company on South Dongjiadu in the Southern City. This is very shocking. After investigation, our company specializes in the wood business and does not engage in the bamboo business, and there is no fact that the Yuchang Bamboo Company is set up in Bailianjing. The report is completely inconsistent with the facts. I hereby request you to correct it to avoid misunderstandings from the outside world. Yours truly, Hu Yuchang Wood Company, January 19, 25th year of the Republic of China.

National Crisis is Increasingly Serious, the Sports Community Should Intensify its Work 174

At this time when the national crisis is increasingly serious, the people of the whole country should pay attention to sports and temper their body and soul. In recent years, our country has vigorously promoted sports and can be said to have done its best. For example, the central government and various provinces and cities have sports administrative staff who specialize in sports affairs. National Games and local primary and secondary school sports meets are held on time. This year, the government will allocate huge funds to participate in the World Games. However, holding various sports competitions is not enough to temper the body and soul of the people in China today. Let us observe that after the war, Germany focused on morning exercises throughout the country and promoted military training in sports, achieving remarkable results. Sports administrative personnel in our country should intensify their work, deeply study the national crisis sports plan, implement it and seek practical results, and hopefully not be biased towards sports competitions. They found him, and the surprise and joy he showed were so natural and frank that few who knew him failed to believe him when he said he knew nothing of the coming or going of the money.

"If I didn't take it, how can I put it back? Please trust me now, and treat me kindly as you always have," he said so pitifully that Amy patted him on the back and said that at least she believed him.

Tommy shook Nat's hand, saying, "So do I, I'm really happy that it wasn't you. But who the devil is it?"

"Now that it's found, let's not bother about it anymore," said Don, gazing at Nat's happy face.

"Ah! I would be like that! I wouldn't want someone to take my things at will and then bring them back, as if by magic," Tommy shouted, looking at his money as if he suspected there was some kind of witchcraft driving it.

Education News

Recent News on the Promotion of Education at All Levels in Guangdong 176

The following is a summary of the recent developments in the promotion of education at all levels in Guangdong Province: "Primary Education" The province, in accordance with the three-year policy plan, urges counties and cities to implement compulsory education. According to reports from various counties, the number of schools has been increasing year by year, and the number of out-of-school children has been gradually decreasing. It also coordinates the overall situation and selects counties that are known to be poor to provide subsidies to help them make adjustments. In the 24th year, the subsidy was increased to more than 120,000 yuan, plus the central government subsidy of 120,000 yuan, and the counties raised more than 500,000 yuan themselves. Statistics show that within the 24th year, a total of 1,130 short-term primary schools must be opened. In addition, the counties must still consider the local conditions and actively promote ordinary primary schools in order to make education universal throughout the province in the shortest possible time to comply with the provisions of the three-year policy plan. "Secondary Education" The province originally had 13 provincial secondary schools, 8 normal schools, and 5 vocational schools. Following the Ministry of Education's order to reduce the number of ordinary secondary schools and promote vocational education and normal education year by year, the province has implemented the order and divided the province into ten normal school districts in accordance with the Ministry's regulations. Vocational schools also follow the district planning of normal school districts. This year, it is planned to add four provincial secondary schools: one provincial Lao Jiang Normal School, two provincial Changsha Normal Schools, three provincial Shantou Fisheries Vocational Schools, and implement the procedure in three phases. The first phase is to set up a fishing department, the second phase is to set up a manufacturing department, and the third phase is to set up an aquaculture department. The 24th year is the second phase to handle the fishing department, enrolling one class each for the senior and junior groups. The province has also set up a provincial sports school to cultivate specialized sports talents, which is divided into three classes: a two-year sports specialty course, enrolling high school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications; a three-year sports normal school course, enrolling junior high school graduates or those with graduates from equivalent schools; and a one-year training course, enrolling current secondary school physical education teachers or those who have worked in professional sports for more than five years. "Higher Education" In order to cultivate high-level industrial technical talents, the province selects government-funded students to study abroad. In addition to the four students who studied in Europe and the United States in the previous year, Huang Guanyue, Tang Yushu, Lu Wen, and Fu Dicai, who were assigned to study papermaking, textile, hydropower, and silk weaving industries, have reported their achievements in the past year. This year (24th year), five students were selected to study abroad: Lin Shihe, specializing in aircraft manufacturing; Huang Yichen, specializing in school building engineering; Zhao Shanhuan, specializing in entomology. The above three students are all sent to the United States. Liu Fukang is sent to the United Kingdom to study shipbuilding, and Huang Dunhan is sent to Japan to study physical education. "Social Education" The Provincial Education Department issued measures for counties and cities to establish public education centers, requiring them to establish public education centers within a time limit as the center of social education in various counties and cities. According to reports from counties and cities, the number of establishments has been increasing year by year. The latest survey shows that Fangcheng has seven, Nanhai and Shunde have five each, Panyu has three, Sanshui and Chaoan have two each, and the remaining 43 counties such as Zhongshan and Shantou City have one each, totaling 68, an increase of about 15 from the previous year. In addition, the villagers in Xinzhao, Panyu County, are mostly engaged in agriculture. Recently, Guangdong Construction set up a sugar factory there, and the nearby residents mostly make a living by planting sugarcane. Local construction has also been flourishing. At the time of the decline of the countryside, psychological construction must be combined with material construction. The Provincial Education Department ordered the Provincial Public Education Center and the Guangzhou District First Sugarcane Construction Site to jointly establish a Public Education Experimental Zone in Rongyong to facilitate the implementation of public education and establish a center for new rural construction, and an experiment has already been established.

Economic Supplement

World Oil Supply and Demand Situation (Continued) 184

— He Bing

World Oil Supply and Demand Situation

Because oil occupies an important position in military industry, the oil industry has developed considerably in all capitalist countries around the world, even when they are experiencing industrial recession. The prosperity or decline of the oil industry depends on the number of various automobiles, airplanes, steamships, etc. In 1931, there were 35,784,000 automobiles in the world. Due to the economic panic, the number of vehicles decreased slightly in the following two years: 33,603,000 in 1932 and 33,331,000 in 1933. Since 1934, due to the urgency of warplanes, the number of various automobiles has increased again, reaching 34,900,000, an increase of 8% compared to 1933, requiring 67,500,000 tons of naphtha, an increase of 6.9% compared to 1933. According to a report by the Paris Business Survey Institute, the index of new light automobile registrations in the four major capitalist countries is as follows (1933 is counted as 100):

Country 1933 1934

United States 136.2 173.3

United Kingdom 119.7 148.3

France 108.1 111.5

Germany 199.5 318.4

Although the demand for oil increased in 1934, there was a contradictory phenomenon: the price of oil fell, especially the price of oil products. The main reason for this is the intensification of national oil self-sufficiency policies and the dumping competition among international oil trusts, which led to an increase in the demand for oil, but the price fell instead. The collapse of the oil market has had the greatest impact on the United States, the world's largest oil producer. Although the government has actively worked to control the oil market and stabilize production, and has issued the Oil Industry Law, its effectiveness is not significant.

In 1934, world oil production increased, with the United States accounting for more than 60% of the world's production. The redistribution of world oil resources and the competition for sales markets among other trusts in the world became increasingly acute. The discovery of the new oil fields in Iraq in 1934 intensified the competition among trusts. On the one hand, countries are developing their own oil industry and oil refining industry, and at the same time, they are preparing for war. The so-called "oil national policy," "oil independence policy," or "oil self-sufficiency policy" is developing rapidly, destroying the original supply and demand relationship in the oil market. The contradiction between overproduction and insufficient oil supply cannot be reconciled, so the demand increases, but the price falls. The trend of world oil production and demand in recent years is as follows:

World Oil Production and Demand

Year Production Amount Index Demand Amount Index Production Exceeds

(Million Tons) (Million Tons) Demand (Million Tons)

Stimulated by the US Oil Industry Law in 1934, the production amount increased greatly. The total production in 1933 and 1934 exceeded the demand by a huge amount of 18.5 million tons.

The fall in the price of world oil products is shown in the following table:

Average Price Index of World Oil Products (1929—100)

Year Paraffin Oil Kerosene Gas Oil Heavy Oil

The Italian Oil Problem

The United States naturally occupies the most important position in today's world oil war, because its production accounts for more than 60% of the world's production, but today, due to the Italian-Abyssinian War, the international oil embargo against Italy has attracted more attention.

Like coal, Italy's oil has been repeatedly prospected by experts, costing the government a lot of public funds. As a result, it has been found that there are no oil resources in the country. Italy only extracts thousands of tons of inferior oil in its own country every year, and the cost is 0.3% higher than ordinary oil. Therefore, Italy has made great efforts to obtain a source of oil supply and ensure that oil will not be lacking in wartime.

Therefore, in order to develop its own oil refining industry, Italy has sought the supply of raw materials from various countries by various means. First, it obtained the exclusive right to exploit local oil from the Albanian government, and then it seized the Romanian oil mining rights. After the discovery of the new oil fields in Iraq, Italy was also a powerful member of the international vested interests.

According to the Italian government's estimate, according to the original plan, 200,000 tons of crude oil can be obtained from Albania by 1936, and 300,000 tons are expected to be imported from Romania, and 400,000 to 500,000 tons can be obtained from Iraq. In this way, Italy can not only use 50% for its own use, but also have a surplus. If this plan is successful, Italy's oil trade policy with various countries will change, that is, it will try its best to increase the import of oil products in order to develop its own oil refining industry and control its own oil market.

In recent years, Italy's oil refining industry has gradually developed. The trend is as follows: (Unit: 1,000 tons) —

In 1934, Italy's oil market was under intense competition from international trusts, and the domestic oil industry was under great pressure, so production decreased significantly. The import of oil products developed annually, as shown in the following table: (Unit: 1,000 tons)

From the above, it can be seen the deep relationship between Italy and other countries in oil trade. It is not easy to achieve the "oil self-sufficiency policy." On January 1, 1935, the quota permit system for the import of oil products was implemented for a period of two years. During this time, the domestic oil industry was actively developed, and a new oil industry law was promulgated in order to develop the domestic industry and achieve self-sufficiency. However, when the Italian-Abyssinian War began in 1925, the oil embargo became a powerful tool in international economic sanctions. If the war continues and countries can truly achieve an oil embargo, Italy's oil panic will inevitably occur.

The oil embargo against Italy has not yet been resolved, and disputes have arisen among the great powers. For example, after the League of Nations notified the oil embargo against Italy on November 18, 1935, the Soviet Union and Romania expressed their approval, while Canada expressed its opposition. The United States, the world's largest oil producer, issued a so-called neutrality, and there is so-called spiritual support for the League of Nations, but there is no concrete decision. However, this matter has aroused great repercussions from the Italian Fascists. For example, the Fascist Grand Council emergency meeting on November 18 last year resolved that if the League of Nations Committee prohibits members from exporting oil, Italy will immediately withdraw from the League of Nations, sever diplomatic relations with the sanctioning countries, and withdraw its ambassadors and consuls. One hundred and twenty-five Italian air force members formed a suicide squad to bomb the essence of the British Navy in the Mediterranean. The air force generals were determined to die, causing the annihilation of the British Mediterranean fleet. Soon, the Italian ambassadors to Britain and France also sent protests, the main point of which was that if Britain and France implemented an oil embargo, Italy would retaliate with acts of war. From this, it can also be seen Italy's panic about oil and the importance of oil in war. After all, Britain is still willing to maintain Italy's original position in Europe and is concerned about the Far East issue. Germany's large-scale rearmament does not want to be too suited to Italy, so the oil embargo is not intended to be realized. (End)

An Analysis of the American Cotton Marketing Cooperative System 185

— Chen Honggen

Cotton is one of the main agricultural products of both China and the United States. In the case of the United States, its cotton production accounts for more than 50% of the world's total, and its annual cotton export value reaches approximately 500 million US dollars, accounting for about 16% of the total export value. In the case of China, cotton production ranks third in the world, with an annual output of about 8 million dan, and exports of about 6-700,000 dan. Taking the year 1933 as an example, cotton exports totaled 723,632 dan, worth 30,238,958 yuan, accounting for 4.94% of the total export value, ranking sixth. Given that the cotton production of these two countries occupies such an important position, the study and improvement of cotton production and marketing systems are essential. Although there are various ways to improve the system in the United States, the cooperative method occupies an important position. Over the past 20 years, through the joint efforts of the government, academic groups, the financial sector, and farmers, remarkable results have been achieved. In contrast, in our country, cotton production has been decreasing in recent years, imports of foreign cotton have surged, production technology has not been reformed at all, and many malpractices have emerged in the marketing system. If this continues, it will inevitably endanger the livelihoods of cotton farmers. The government authorities and enlightened people are aware of this, and have therefore jointly sought ways to remedy the situation. The Cotton Industry Control Committee, the Cotton Production Improvement Institutes in various provinces, the North China Agricultural Improvement Society, and the cotton marketing cooperatives established in various places have emerged one after another. However, cotton production improvement cannot be achieved in a short period of time, while the improvement of cotton marketing is easier to achieve. The various malpractices in the American cotton marketing system before its reform were very similar to those in our country. Moreover, their cooperative marketing system to remedy these malpractices has some aspects that can be applied to our country. I have collected relevant information on American cotton cooperative marketing and compiled it into this article, hoping to provide a reference for those in China engaged in the cotton industry.

(1) Shortcomings of the Original American Cotton Marketing System

To understand the American cotton marketing cooperation system, it is necessary to first explore the shortcomings of its original system. The following are the main points:

(A) Ginning

(1) Ginning Costs: Most cotton farmers do not have their own ginning machines, and after collecting the cotton, they send it to privately-run ginning factories to be ginned into lint cotton. The purpose of ginning factories is to make a profit, so they inevitably increase ginning costs as much as possible. Every 100 pounds of seed cotton requires about 30 to 50 US cents. Cottonseeds are considered too little in quantity by cotton farmers, so they often do not ask the factories for them, and the factories accumulate a small amount into a large amount, which can also generate extra income.

(2) Ginning Quality: The machines used in privately-run ginning factories are mostly decayed, and their efficiency is reduced. During ginning, they often fail to clearly separate the cotton lint from the cottonseeds, and sometimes even mix in unclean substances such as mud and sand, reducing the quality of the lint cotton and thus damaging the cotton's selling price.

(B) Failure to Grade Cotton Quality: At the beginning of cotton sales, there was no such thing as grading. Transactions were based only on samples. Later, as cotton textile factories became more developed, they needed cotton of uniform quality for weaving various cotton textiles. Therefore, grading methods gradually emerged in the cotton market. However, in the beginning, the grading was arbitrary and without fixed standards. Buyers often deliberately lowered the grade of the cotton they purchased to gain an advantage, which easily caused disputes between the two parties. In 1923, the Bureau of Agricultural Economics of the U.S. Department of Agriculture (U.S.D.A) formulated a Universal Cotton Standard Act. Based on the results of the cotton market, it was proven that Middling Cotton was the highest grade. Cotton above this grade could not be sold at a higher price. Under this marketing system, cotton farmers would not be willing to produce long-staple cotton to increase their burden. Because the shorter the cotton lint, the lower the production cost than that of long-staple cotton, and the yield of lint cotton is higher than that of long-staple cotton. If cotton prices are not based on the quality of the cotton, then cotton farmers will inevitably compete to plant short-staple cotton, and the quality of the cotton will decline daily.

(C) Profiteering by Middlemen: From the producer to the consumer, cotton passes through many levels, including ginners, cotton merchants, cotton shops, cotton brokers, cotton warehouses, and consignment stores. Each stage is exploited once, so the cotton price received by cotton farmers is reduced.

(D) Adulteration and Cheating of Cotton: If cotton farmers sell seed cotton to ginners, then they intentionally leave a gap in the machine during ginning to make an unexpected income. Some also add water to the lint cotton, with the maximum addition being 20% to 30%. Even if the ginners do not cheat in this way, when the cotton is transferred to other middlemen, they will inevitably cheat in this way.

The above-mentioned malpractices are only the major ones, but they are already enough to show the urgency of reform. The cooperative marketing system thus emerged. According to the American cotton transport cooperative organization, there are two types: state cooperatives and the national federation (i.e., the American Cotton Growers Exchange). The following describes their general situation in order:

(2) State Cotton Marketing Cooperatives

(A) Principles and Policies: State cotton marketing cooperatives are all non-stock, non-profit societies. Cooperatives are purely service-oriented and do not require equipment that consumes huge amounts of money. All transportation costs, insurance fees, interest, operating expenses, etc., are shared according to the amount of cotton delivered by the members. Most cooperative members are limited to residents of a certain region or a certain state. Sometimes, only members of certain special farmer groups can join. For example, the Arkansas Cotton Production and Marketing Cooperative must limit membership to members of the Farmers' Association. Members need to pay a membership fee to join the cooperative. Some stipulate that ten yuan must be paid at one time, while others stipulate that 25 cents per bale should be charged for each individual's sales volume. In addition, two contracts need to be signed: one is the organizational contract, which states the purpose and principles of the organization, the operating plan, membership qualifications, etc.; the other is the sales contract or agreement, which contains the responsibilities, rights, and terms of the parties signing the contract. If a member breaches the contract and fails to deliver the stipulated cotton, the cooperative will impose a fine of three to ten cents per pound. The contract term is mostly five years. The previous IronClad Contract stipulated that members could not freely withdraw from the cooperative during the contract period. Later, it was revised so that those who wish to withdraw from the cooperative must notify the cooperative in writing before the second Wednesday of May each year. After verification and approval by the person in charge, the contractual relationship can be terminated.

(B) Structure and Management: State cooperatives are centralized, with only one central organization. No branches are established in various localities, but the regions under their jurisdiction are divided into several districts, each with an office. All contract signing and ginning factories and warehouses established in the area are directly managed by the cooperative. The management agency of the cooperative is the board of directors. The directors are elected by farmers in each district. The method is to first conduct a preliminary election in each district, and then elect directors from the representatives. Each member has only one vote to prevent manipulation. All directors are unpaid, but they are given a reasonable allowance for travel expenses during meetings. In addition to the board of directors, three to five members are designated to form a committee to execute daily affairs. The cooperative has one chairman, one vice-chairman, and one secretary-accountant each. In order to improve operating efficiency, the cooperative is specially divided into accounting, finance, marketing, and service departments, each with a department head responsible for handling matters.

(C) Operating Methods: (1) Collecting Flowers and Sampling: During the cotton picking season, offices in various districts send collectors to collect cotton from cotton farmers and transport it to the nearest squeezing plant (Cinoress). The office sends people to take samples to identify their grades. If cotton farmers urgently need money, they can borrow a certain amount of cotton prices at this time. Another method is for members to pack the cotton themselves and send it directly to the warehouse designated by the cooperative, or hand it over to the railway bureau to transport it to the designated warehouse. The warehouse manager takes one sample on each side of each bale. All samples are sent to the cooperative's head office, and the cooperative hires trained and licensed Cotton Classers to grade them and issue grade certificates. The cooperative then combines samples of the same grade in one place and registers the number of bales of each grade delivered by each member.

(2) Storage—Cotton is a durable agricultural product, so its trading period is longer. If it can be properly stored and evaluated at a price, then a greater profit can be obtained. Most state cotton marketing cooperatives in the United States do not build their own warehouses, but rent them from private warehouses. The reason is that the cost of building warehouses is too high. The equipment and efficiency of private warehouses are already very complete. Using the cooperative's strength to negotiate prices with them can get more favorable terms. If there is not enough cotton for storage, then it cannot be fully utilized, wasting financial resources.

(3) Regulating Finance: The expenses required by cooperatives can be divided into three main categories:

(1) Operating expenses of the marketing organization—can be further divided into permanent equipment expenses (such as houses and utensils, etc.) and recurring operating expenses (such as salaries, commissions, etc.). The former are appropriated from the public reserve fund extracted according to the sales volume, and the latter are funded by the commissions paid by the members.

(2) Expenses required for marketing activities—such as member advances on cotton value, transportation costs, etc. The amount required depends on the number of bales of cotton received, the percentage of advance cotton value, the level of market prices, and the level of freight rates. Since the cooperative is a non-stock organization, it must borrow money from banks or government agencies, using cotton warehouse receipts and bills of lading as collateral.

(3) Assistance to members in production or other aspects—Most cotton farmers in the southern United States are tenant farmers with very little capital of their own. They feel powerless to purchase fertilizers and seeds during cotton production, and mostly purchase production supplies on credit from local merchants or borrow money from small banks, using green seedlings as collateral. The cooperative must provide financial assistance to these members to relieve their difficulties. To meet this need, each cooperative establishes an affiliated financial company, issues stocks to raise funds, and lends them to members.

(4) Sales and Calculation of Loans: The cooperative has a marketing department, headed by an experienced person, or an affiliated company is established to operate independently. There are two methods of selling cotton by the cooperative. The first is mixed sales, also known as the pooling method, which combines cotton of the same grade from members, and sells it successively until the end of a pooling period (one day, one week, one month, one year, etc.). The average price per bale is obtained by dividing the total number of bales of cotton of each grade by the total sales price of each grade, and then distributing it according to the number of bales of cotton of each grade delivered by each member. (However, various deductible expenses need to be deducted first.) The second is the individual sales method. The member who delivers the cotton determines its sales period and minimum price, and accepts the remaining cotton price after deducting transportation and sales costs. However, this method is to accommodate cotton farmers who are unwilling to join the pooling method. After cotton farmers recognize the benefits of pooling, they all wish to abandon their opinions. Therefore, individual sales have been gradually reduced. The targets of cotton sales are major cotton textile factories at home and abroad. The cooperative sends agents to major cotton markets to be responsible for sales. Since the establishment of the American Cotton Growers Exchange, many state cooperatives have entrusted it to sell on their behalf.

(5) Ginning: The malpractices of private ginning factories have been described in detail earlier. However, cooperatives' operation of the ginning industry is to be completed last. Because it is a centralized organization, local cooperative ginning factories are supervised and directed by the head office, which sends people to manage them. Cotton farmers only have the right to use them. The location of the ginning factories must take into account the amount of cotton ginned and the distance from the members. Members who submit seed cotton for ginning also charge a small fee. From a cooperative point of view, the effectiveness of ginning factories is quite great. Because in a centralized organization, the distance between members and the cooperative is very far, and there is no spiritual maintenance. If cooperative ginning factories can be established in rural areas or towns, then farmers' relationship with the cooperative will be closer and their faith will be deeper. Moreover, ginning factories can also be used as places to collect cotton, replacing the location of squeezing plants. After ginning into lint cotton, samples are taken and then packaged and transported to warehouses, to avoid the trouble of sampling in the future.

(3) American Cotton Growers Exchange

After the establishment of state cotton marketing cooperatives, there was still no joint organization to standardize the marketing system and assist in the marketing operations of various cooperatives. The Texas and Oklahoma cooperatives first created this type of organization, and held an inaugural meeting in 1921, named the American Cotton Growers Exchange. At that time, a total of twelve state cooperatives joined. The following describes its general situation:

(A) Principles and Organization: This exchange, like the state cooperatives, is a non-stock, non-profit organization. It has no articles of association or bylaws, and only maintains its transactions based on the contracts signed when members join the society. The exchange has a total of twelve departments: (1) Administration and Execution Department, (2) Management Department, (3) Classification and Standards Department, (4) Lending Department, (5) Insurance Department, (6) Transportation Department, (7) Finance Department, (8) Statistics Department, (9) General Cotton Sales Department, (10) Fine Cotton Sales Department, (11) Legal Department, (12) Field Service Department. The general office is located in Memphis, Tennessee.

(B) Management: The exchange has a board of directors, composed of three people elected by each cooperative. They are re-elected every year. In addition, the government appoints three public directors to protect public interests. The board of directors meets twice or three times a year, convened by the chairman, to determine operating policies according to the provisions of the contract. In addition, there is an executive committee, composed of one representative from each society. It meets once a month and is responsible for carrying out all affairs. The society has one chairman, one vice-chairman, and one secretary-accountant each.

(C) Business: The business undertaken by the exchange can be divided into four major categories:

(1) Sales: State cooperatives that feel that sales are not widespread, or that have excessive amounts and are unable to sell them, can entrust the exchange to sell on their behalf. The exchange has agents in major cotton markets at home and abroad, who report on market conditions at all times and represent the exchange in negotiating transactions. State cooperatives can thus save the labor of sales.

(2) Regulating Finance—The exchange can use its strong influence to negotiate loans with major banks to resolve the financial difficulties of state cooperatives. However, when a loan is established, the state cooperatives must directly sign a contract with the lender. The exchange is only in the position of a mediator.

(3) Field Services—The service department of the exchange specializes in investigating the operating methods of state cooperatives, learning from each other's strengths and promoting them widely, so that each society can gradually adopt uniform and perfect methods. In addition, it assists the service departments of state cooperatives in developing their society affairs.

(4) Statistics—This is the work most valued by the branches of the exchange, that is, collecting cotton transport figures in the market, such as supply, consumption, long-term trends in cotton prices, seasonal changes in cotton prices, etc., analyzing them, and reporting them to the state cotton marketing cooperatives. State cooperatives can predict the relationship between supply and demand in the market and determine their sales policies.

(D) Operating Methods: All state cooperatives organized according to pure cooperative principles can register with the exchange. After approval by the executive committee, they can sign a contract with the society, designate three representatives as directors, and one person as an executive committee member. The procedures are completed. Thereafter, if there is cotton that can be entrusted to the exchange to sell on its behalf, and they can enjoy other rights. The exchange's expenses are very low. All sales expenses are divided according to the number of bales of cotton delivered by each society, and a small commission is collected for the society's expenses.

The above is only a brief description of the American cotton marketing cooperation system. As for its advantages and disadvantages, due to space limitations, they cannot be described in detail. I will write a supplementary note another day.

Finance: Financial Clearing Procedures are More Complicated 186

Yesterday, the financial market was as calm as usual. Although the closing period is imminent, there is no sign of tightening. Banks are lending as much as possible and accommodating overdrafts. The market situation is therefore loose, and the closing period can be passed safely. However, the clearing procedures are more complicated. The overnight interest rate remains at the original price, unchanged from beginning to end, both morning and afternoon at eight percent. In overnight transactions, morning market transfers were more than 3.8 million, new transactions were more than 60 million, afternoon market transactions were more than 400,000, and small general meeting transactions were more than 800,000. Bank collections were made on a holiday schedule. The Shanghai Native Bank Clearing House received more than 48 million yuan in collection notes. In subsidiary currency transactions, the morning market traded 130,000 jiao of Guangdong small silver coins, and the afternoon market traded 40,000 jiao. The black market rate was 11.8 jiao, down 1 li from the previous day. 29,400 strings of copper coins were traded, worth 9,800 legal tender yuan.

Securities: Rumors of Interest Rate Reduction and Postponement Hit the Bond Market Suddenly; Shorts Took Advantage of the Pressure; Military Bonds Fell More Than Six Yuan 187

From January 13th to 18th last week, speculation on the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange was intense, leading to extraordinary changes. After rumors of interest rate reductions and postponements, short sellers were extremely enthusiastic, especially those releasing forward contracts. Therefore, forward prices were lower than spot prices. The difference often exceeded the principal and interest earned each month. Normally, arbitrage transactions would roll over to the next month when they expired, involving tens of millions, and market prices would be maintained as a result. However, with the rumors of interest rate reductions and the unfavorable market prices, nearly all arbitrageurs in the market delivered their contracts this month. After the September 18th Incident, although market prices were small, the profit from hedging was very high, and a portion of investment still absorbed spot contracts. Currently, investors, except for a few retail investors, have almost disappeared from the market. Most of the market transactions are speculation. The big players on both the short and long sides are evenly matched. The shorts use rumors to deliberately make forward prices lower than spot prices, so that arbitrageurs naturally leave the market. It has already driven the important elements of investment out of the market, reducing the strength of the opposing side, and deliberately using various rumors, they are determined to make the longs yield. It can be seen that they also feel that they are too big to fail and cannot compensate. Because they rely on the interest rate reduction issue, if it is not true, then the future reaction will be even more extraordinary. The longs believe that the government stated that after the September 18th and January 28th incidents in 1932, when bond interest rates were reduced and postponed, the decision would be permanent. Moreover, even if the interest rate is reduced, it would only increase the government's income by more than one million yuan per month. Is there no other way to compensate? They must shake the bond market. If the rumor is that new bonds are being issued in exchange for old bonds, regardless of whether the interest rate and term of the new bonds are consistent with the original ones, if the interest rate is reduced and the term is extended, then the shorts who are currently shorting will definitely not be in this case. In the future, rolling over will result in huge losses. If they re-compensate, it will be easier for the longs to surround them. The above sections are indeed the actual pain of both sides recently, so there are rumors of mediators persuading both sides to settle out of court, but it is not easy to comply. Today is the last day of the year, and there will be a week's holiday afterwards, so there will be extremely large changes on this day. Investing and speculating are both once-in-a-lifetime opportunities, but unfortunately, not all can fully understand the crux of the problem. On the Saturday and Sunday of last week, retail investors covered their shorts on Wednesday, and the prices rose by a few jiao to one or two yuan. The remaining days were all under the pressure of the shorts, and the market prices gradually declined. The rumors of interest rate reductions became more and more true, but no formal announcement was ever seen, and whether it actually happened or not, the market rumors all aimed at this point as the only goal. Ticket holders and the financial community across the country are panicked. On Thursday, the Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to Beijing requesting an announcement, which boosted morale. In the end, the rumors did not have good results, and market prices rose and fell, still trending downward. After that, market prices felt more and more unsustainable, and on Friday, they fell by about two and a half yuan. Saturday was the most serious period for rumors of interest rate reductions. Military bonds and Nine Goodness bonds suddenly fell to the limit. The market sentiment was extremely weak, but those who went long were not very flustered, and especially retail investors were very interested in eating in. The competition between the long and short sides has reached its peak, and it will soon be unveiled. Let us wait and see. The result of the week's market prices was a fall of at least more than one yuan, and the most fell by as much as six and a half yuan. The total number of transactions totaled 15,831,000 yuan. Piece Goods - Woolen Fabrics: Substantial Trading in Stockpiled Goods 191

Last Saturday, the woolen fabric market saw only sporadic business from storefront dealers. Otherwise, there was little formal trading. As the end-of-year closing approached, both buyers and sellers were focused on inventory and settling accounts, so attendance at the public market was sparse. However, behind the scenes, dealers were actively trading stockpiled goods. Shops facing tight credit secretly offered discounted prices, while those with ample funds absorbed as much stock as possible. Both insiders and outside speculators showed considerable appetite, leading to numerous under-the-table deals.
