Snippets 192

— (Nai Ling)

We all live in a house. Who wants this roof to collapse? If you don't want the roof to collapse, of course, all the pillars and beams must be repaired and strengthened. If that's not enough, more supports should be added to hold up the roof. If you harbor wishful thinking, waiting until the roof collapses to take action, then perhaps everyone will perish in that instant when the roof collapses!

"If you don't advance, you retreat." This is an old saying, originally used in the context of sailing. However, I believe that applying this old saying to other matters is still valuable. For example, if you are sick, if you do not quickly seek medical treatment, the illness will never heal. It will only become more serious day by day without you realizing it! Or, for example, with learning, if you do not actively study and research, you will not only fail to progress, but what you have already learned will gradually be forgotten and lost. Friends, remember this famous saying: "If you don't advance, you retreat" is the law of evolution for all things!

School Sickness 193

— Shui Rong

The United States has recently discovered a type of school sickness, said to be a product unique to schools. Sufferers are usually elementary school students, often exhibiting characteristics such as anger, anxiety, agitation, and a heightened emotional state; they also have weak stomachs, restless sleep, and frequent nightmares. These symptoms appear after the start of the school year and worsen as the semester progresses. Mental tests and athletic competitions accelerate its development.

The root of this neurosis lies in the suppression of children who are already somewhat neurotic. Many school systems require children to complete the same subjects at the same pace. Otherwise, the "remarks" section will be filled with words like "D grade," "stupid," "dull," or "inferior." Relatively more neurotic children struggle to keep up with their peers in one or two subjects and, under the encouragement of teachers, push themselves, resulting in a disease filled with sorrow.

A group of health experts is paying attention to this diagnosed illness. Some advocate that report cards should only state "satisfactory" or "unsatisfactory." Others believe that schools should fundamentally eradicate the demon of "suppression."

Seeing this news, I am truly happy for the children in the United States. I only hope that those experts will soon develop concrete prevention methods. Following that, of course, I have to think of my own many younger siblings! They are growing up quietly, without attracting any attention or interest. So if their grades are not good, they can be ordered to stand in the corner, attend night school, or be denied food when boarding. They are scolded as "dunce," "slowpoke." At the end of the semester, the teachers consider their responsibility fulfilled by writing "inferior" on the report card. And the fathers, after receiving the report, cannot avoid being furious: on one hand, they are pained by the wasted money without any return; on the other hand, they start to abuse their children in the manner of "it is the father's fault if he raises them without instruction," reducing their material comforts in the hope that they will become self-aware?

If many children in China also suffer from school sickness, who would discover it and pay attention to it? Ah, save the children!

A-Grade Milk 194

— Zhou Xian

There was a female student at a certain university who was once hailed as a queen. At that time, the general student body gave her a nickname: "A-Grade Milk."

It is said that the nickname "A-Grade Milk" has a bit of a story behind it. The reason is that the old gentleman, the female student's grandfather, started his business by raising cows. The family was in a certain colony in the South. There, they kept 200 dairy cows. A-Grade Milk had been drinking milk produced on their own farm since she was young. For more than ten years, she had never been sick, so that kind of healthy and beautiful physique was just like the A-Grade Milk in the milk shed, so it met the standard. So calling her A-Grade Milk was indeed the most accurate thing to say.

When A-Grade Milk was studying at that university, she would always drink one pound of A-Grade Milk a day. It was said that she had been drinking it for more than ten years, so she had to drink it. But her drinking of milk, it is said, did not require her to reach into her own pocket. Even all the other expenses outside of milk were all covered by a certain student, Mr. Ouyang. So the generous Mr. Ouyang got the nickname of "milk shed owner." Mr. Ouyang also regarded himself as the boss of the milk shed. He absolutely did not allow anyone else to touch A-Grade Milk.

After studying at the university for two years, the milk shed owner reached his boiling point. The lovers finally became husband and wife and finally got married. So A-Grade Milk dropped out of school and followed the boss back south to live a sweet life.

This was a story from the summer vacation of the year before last. After that, A-Grade Milk's news was quiet, and almost all the students forgot about her. But in the autumn of last year, A-Grade Milk was suddenly found again at another university. She had disappeared and no longer had the spotlight of the past. At first, everyone didn't know that this was A-Grade Milk from a certain university, but after two or three months, the secret was finally revealed. According to well-informed sources, A-Grade Milk and the boss divorced only half a year after they got married, so now A-Grade Milk has returned to the qualification of a young lady.

But A-Grade Milk, after experiencing trauma, gave up all pleasure in life and buried herself in her studies, not having any boyfriends, and became a good student who couldn't work any harder. So a group of mischievous old classmates changed her nickname to B-Grade Milk, saying that she was no longer as captivating as she used to be.

Little Western Paradise 196

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Third: High Talk Resounds in the Air, Lawsuit to be Filed, Old Friends Reconnect Over Wine, Profit Can Be Forgotten

But then again, unless he completely backs down, he has to find a proper way to resolve this. Besides filing a lawsuit, what else is there? Thinking just like that, if he is going to file a lawsuit, then he doesn't need to be afraid of offending them. He heard laughter upstairs, women's voices, wasn't that the commissioner's wife? She laughed, "If you lose this lawsuit here, appeal to the High Court. If you lose in the High Court, appeal to the Supreme Court in Nanjing. Even if you lose in the Supreme Court in Nanjing, it will be a year later. You're a free person, what are you afraid of getting tangled up with him for? In this year, you can eat, drink, and dress without worry. We're all here to help you." The voice carried downstairs, still so clear. The person speaking seemed to be doing it on purpose. Jia Duocai went back into his room, lit a cigarette, lay diagonally on the bed with his legs propped up on a stool, and kept thinking about what tactics he needed to use to deal with them. He suddenly said to himself, "I've seen all kinds of storms, am I going to be intimidated by them?" So he jumped up and, using the paper, ink, brush, and inkstone that were already on the table, drafted a letter: "Editor, I have decided to hire a lawyer and formally file a lawsuit for the sake of my personal integrity. Please write about my case based on this, and do not need to worry about anything else. Sincerely, Jia Duocai." After writing the letter, he looked outside the door to see if there was a tea boy. He wanted to call a tea boy to send the letter. Then he saw the tea boy leading two people to the room next door. One of them was a large, fat man wearing a long and large blue silk robe, chewing on more than half a cigar, holding a straw hat and a cane in his hand, looking quite like an Eastern capitalist. The tea boy opened the door for him and led him in, and he heard him say in a complaining tone, "Who said the people of Xi'an don't know how to do business? They are much more cunning than us Easterners." Then a local replied, "Aren't we honest? If we were tricky, we would keep this land for a few more months and sell it after the train line is open, wouldn't we make even more [omitted]." Jia Duocai was most interested in these kinds of words, so he withdrew into the room and sat down, turning his face to listen. (893)

Daytime Nap 201

— Yang Zuozhou

I can't sleep at night, everything is silent, but my thoughts are surging.

Qi Dong Ye Yu says, "The poisonous snake of worries sleeps in your heart; only when the sleeping snake leaves can you sleep peacefully." But the poisonous snakes of worries in my heart are too numerous and difficult to completely remove.

Insomniacs are sleepy during the day, but the work is demanding, and they can't take a nap. I occasionally read Lu Fangweng's poem about daytime naps, "Sleeping together in a ball tastes long, host and guest forget each other; soon the guest leaves and the host wakes up, the same west window has no setting sun."

And Wu Sengyougui's poem, "Reading has strained my brow, but lying down brings joy to my bones; when I wake up, I don't know if it's early or late, and little of the setting sun remains in the west window."

I think that if I could get half a day off and sleep to my heart's content, it would be the greatest pleasure in life. Even if I am ridiculed as rotten wood and dung, I would not care.

But this is ultimately an elegant hobby for those of the privileged class, and a poor scholar does not have this blessing.

Congee Shop 202

— Wang Zhiqin

The congee shop is the cheapest place to fill one's stomach. With a dozen or so copper coins, you can go in and come out with a full belly.

Shanghai has a large population of rich and poor residents, so the congee shops are everywhere you look. Except for closing for the first three days of the lunar new year, they are open day and night, rain or shine. Many [omitted] who don't have a proper home see the congee shop as a place to stay without paying for a room. Every night when the road is empty, you can go in and order a few bowls of thin congee to rest your feet. In this cold winter, if you know the waiter well, you can greet him and lie face down on the table, using it as a temporary residence. It seems that the congee shop's open-door policy is undoubtedly a charitable organization that shelters the poor. I hope that Shanghai's businessmen will open more small congee shops and fewer large hotels, so that homeless wanderers will have more places to stay at night.

Talks

Demands on Dramatists in the National Salvation Movement 215

— Traveler from Oka

Due to the critical situation in North China, after the call for the national salvation movement was issued from Beiping, the cultural city that is the "hometown of the May Fourth Movement," it immediately received a strong response from the people of various regions. The citizens of Shanghai quickly organized national salvation groups. People from the cultural world, women, elementary school teachers, nurses, ... to people from various professional circles, all rose up to participate in this determined national salvation action, tragically demonstrating that the national spirit of China has not yet subsided, and moreover, it will never subside. Chinese people, except for traitors and national sellouts, none want to be slaves of a conquered nation, watching as our territory is lost, whether directly or indirectly (in disguise)! Therefore, despite the current "good neighborly relations" and various difficulties, the sentiment of the popular national salvation movement is still rising day by day, more fervent than any period since the September 18th Incident!

In this urgent situation, in the rising cry for national salvation, the cultural world, which has always stood at the forefront of the times, should stand even further ahead of the masses and shoulder the task of the national salvation movement. However, judging from the current situation, the people of the cultural world have clearly not fulfilled their responsibilities. As the declaration of the Shanghai Cultural Circles National Salvation Association says: "... Teachers at all levels across the country have not stood in front of the students and taken on the responsibility of leading students to save the nation; people engaged in journalism are still concealing reality and reversing right and wrong under the news censorship system, and have not stood in front of the masses and taken on the leadership of public opinion; magazine editors and writers have not done their best to use their conscience and their pens to speak for the masses and guide their actions; others, such as workers in publishing, drama, film, and other departments, have also failed to fulfill their duties within their respective fields. This cannot but be said to be our shame." Indeed, our cultural people should immediately wash away these shames and immediately take on our urgent tasks. Therefore, here, I should mention the drama department and the dramatists engaged in theatrical activities.

Last year's theatrical activity was very active, and therefore, last year was worthy of being called the "year of drama." Judging from the situation at the beginning of this year, the theatrical activity this year will generally not be lower than last year. However, this year is a year of crisis, and theatrical performances must seize the current urgent situation. At the end of last year, I said in "Talks": "If we do not want to be conquered and do not want to be slaves of a conquered nation, then drama can be said to be a powerful weapon for us in the national independence and liberation movement!" However, current dramatists have not actively used this powerful weapon, which cannot but be said to be our shame. From the newspapers, we vaguely hear news of students in Beiping going to the countryside to conduct propaganda, and some people are putting on some anti-imperialist dramas with rudimentary conditions. The students are not professional dramatists, but they can seize the current situation to do drama. On the other hand, looking back at the Shanghai dramatists who are professional, they have not actively stirred up their energy, and some even perform some unimportant plays. This really makes us feel great sorrow! And feel boundless shame! ...

After the September 18th Incident, anti-imperialist drama was active for a period of time. The current situation is much more critical than the September 18th Incident, but why have the dramatists become silent instead? In order to save our country, save our nation, and make the Chinese masses the masters of their own country; we demand that dramatists unite together in the united front of the national salvation movement, regardless of the form of the play, regardless of the faction, ... all should unite to perform anti-imperialist national salvation dramas, so that the Chinese masses can see the roar of our nation on the stage, arouse the enthusiasm for national salvation, and promote the development of the entire national salvation movement. - On the stage, let us shout: "Roar, China!"

Between Profession and Unemployment 216

— Tang

When I learned that Junyi was going to be sent to Qingjiangpu, my colleagues and I held a final gathering in a restaurant. Junyi was unusually excited and drank an excessive amount of wine. He said, "This is really unexpected, but I feel this responsibility is too great. For twenty-five years, I have not left Shanghai a single step. Now I am going to the strange northern region alone. I don't know how to deal with those cunning merchants?" But he continued, "This is a broad road in front of me, I must work hard!"

Junyi was one of the most congenial among our graduating classmates. After graduation, he was recommended by his uncle to work in a compradore's office in a foreign firm. The compradore was a close friend of his uncle, and the condition for the recommendation was to learn, so Junyi did not have a fixed title in the compradore's office: whenever the compradore thought of something that needed him to do, he would order him to do it. Naturally, many things went beyond the scope of a general employee. Junyi was very dissatisfied with this "errand boy" position. He thought that the compradore was not sincere in accommodating him, but was relying on his uncle.
